### creation, elements, transformation
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/D1giBxi2ovc?t=0
**Verse References:** SB 2.5.26-29
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The whole process of creation is an act of gradual evolution and development from one element to another reaching up to the variegatedness of the earth."
**Summary:** The speaker reads verses from Srimad Bhagavatam describing the transformation of elements in the process of creation.

Om Namo Bhagavate Vasudevaya. Reading from Srimad Bhagavatam, Canto 2, Chapter 5, Verses 26-29. I will read myself. Reading from Srimad Bhagavatam, Canto 2, Chapter 5, Verses 26-29. Because the star is transformed, the air is generated with the quality of touch. And by previous succession of the air is also full of sound and the basic principle of duration of life, sense perception, mental power, and bodily strength. When the air is transformed in course of time and nature's course, fire is generated, taking shape with the sense of touch and sound. Since fire is also transformed, there is a manifestation of water full of juice and taste. As previously, it also has form and touch and is also full of sound. And water being transformed from all life on Earth appears knew in order and as previously becomes qualitatively full of juice, touch, sound and form respectively.

### creation, elements, sense perception
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/D1giBxi2ovc?t=149
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The qualities of sense perception are fully represented in the earth and they are manifested in other elements to a lesser extent."
**Summary:** The speaker continues reading from the Srimad Bhagavatam, elaborating on the qualities of elements and their relationship to sense perception, emphasizing the role of air and the benefits of yogic exercises.

Aged 15 years. Burokar Katanyankaha, from thesavravabhyan gods, Baba Akram, Maharaja Sakyamundrya. Based on this bogotan image, light, the world and consciousness are not turned towards one conspicuous feeling effected by the devils. Avarikasat jna kya ajanya jna jnakatseya? As we will. The whole process of creation is an act of gradual evolution and development from one. HomКyaka kttur. The whole process of creation is an act of gradual evolution and development from one element to another reaching up to the variegatedness of the earth as so many trees, plants, mountains, rivers, reptiles, birds, animals, and varieties of human being. The quality of sense perception is also evolutionary, namely generated from sound, then touch and form, from touch to form, taste and order are also generated along with the gradual development of strife, air, fire, water, and earth. They are all mutually the cross and effect of one another, but the original cross is the Lord himself in plenary portion as Maha Vishnu lying in the trouser water of the Mahat Tattva. As such, Lord Krishna is described in Brahma Samhita as the cross of all crosses, and this is confirmed in the Vajra Dhrita 10.8 as follows: The qualities of sense perception are fully represented in the earth and they are manifested in other elements to a lesser extent. In the strife there is sound only, whereas in the air there are sound and touch, in the fire there are sound, touch, and shape, and in the water there is taste also along with the other perceptions, namely sound, touch, and shape. In the earth, however, there are all the above mentioned qualities with an extra development of order also. Therefore, on the earth there is a full display of variegatedness of life which is originally started with the basic principle of air. Diseases of the body take place due to degenerate, due to derangement of air within the earthly body of the living being. Mental disease result from special derangement of the air within the body, and as such yodit exercise is especially beneficial to keep the air in order so that diseases of the body becomes almost nil by such exercise when they are properly done. The duration of life is also in traces and one can have control over death also by such practices. A perfect yoti can have command over death and treat the body at the right moment when he is competent to transfer himself to a suitable planet. The birthday yodi however surpasses all the yodit yodis because by dint of his devotional service he is promoted to the region beyond the material sky and is placed in one of the planets in the spiritual strike by supreme will of the Lord, the controller of everything. So.

### creation, drama, roles
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/D1giBxi2ovc?t=372
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "We are all the living entities, actors, and we have to play our role, some as men, some as women, some intelligent men, some foolish men, some intelligent women, some not so intelligent women, all kinds."
**Summary:** The speaker uses the analogy of a film director and actors to explain the roles of Lord Brahma and living entities in the creation, emphasizing that we are all actors playing different roles in this cosmic drama.

The process of creation is being described in this chapter. The chapter is called the cause of all causes. So in this verse we are seeing today how sky is transformed, air is transformed, air is generated and air has the some of the qualities of touch and sound and so on. So actually this is a description and then we saw how from air, air and other different perceptions also come about. Suppose let's say I'm a film director and I'm planning a film, and in that film I want some of you to become the king, some of you to become the Queen, some of you to become warriors, some of you to become an invader villain who will come and do all nonsense, all wrong things, and some of you soldiers. And so now in filmmaking there is the one important step after the script, casting all that is done, that's called set design because it's a story of a king, queen, all this, we need a palace, we need a battleground, we need horses, we need elephants, we need soldiers. Next as a film director I'll start planning all of this so that when we turn on the lights and all of you can act out very correctly. King will play his role, Queen will play her role, and then the invader will come and all the different things will as per the story will unfold. So in the same way, Lord Brahma who is the director of this universe, creator of the universe, he is doing the set design as we read in the Bhagavatam. So we are all the living entities, actors, and we have to play our role, some as men, some as women, some intelligent men, some foolish men, some intelligent women, some not so intelligent women, all kinds. And for this drama to unfold, we need homes, we need buildings, we need plants, trees, planets. So Brahma is creating all of this.

### drama, illusion, identity

**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Very rarely people think, they are all busy with their roles, they have to play mother, father, husband, wife, and they want to play it out nicely so that everybody is impressed with the role I am playing."
**Summary:** The speaker poses the question of why we are part of this cosmic drama, explaining that although it feels real, it is temporary like a cinema, and people are generally preoccupied with playing their roles without questioning the purpose.

So a fundamental question is, why are we all part of this drama? But this is like a, this, okay, that's like a drama, cinema is all right, but this looks like real life. This doesn't look like drama. No, actually it is a fact. What is a drama, what is a cinema? After some time, the curtains will close and the lights are turned off and drama ends. So even in our lives, one day curtain will be drawn, lights will be turned off, our drama will end, but it doesn't appear like that. It looks like real, you know, this is my wife, this is my husband, this is my home, this is my father, this is my mother, these are my children, this is my house. Why all of this has come about? These are deeper questions. One is you are a king, play properly your role as a king, you Queen play properly Queen as a role as a queen, do your proper, be a strong king, all that is one thing, but a very fundamental deeper question is why have I become an actor in this drama? But very rarely people think, they are all busy with their roles, they have to play mother, father, husband, wife, and they want to play it out nicely so that everybody is impressed with the role I am playing. We rarely think why this drama is going on and why have I become part of this drama, what is all this?

So here from the Vedic literatures we get an understanding of this. We are all spirit souls, just like in the drama or in the cinema there is set designer and makeup artist, costume designer. The costume designer will design for the king, you have to play the role of a king so you should look like a king, you she must look like a queen, all the costume design will happen, palace is built, Brahma is doing all this, you should get a male body, you should get a female body, you should look like this, you should look like this, trees, plants, but inside this body is the spirit soul. We are the spirit soul, we are playing the role of a man, of a woman, of an animal, of a bird for some time and then the drama ends and then we will be an actor. After he finishes one drama he'll get commissioned to do another drama so we will get another opportunity, we will go to another situation. Now the Vedic literatures provides a very very significant perspective why have we become part of this drama, what is this going on and that is we are all spirit souls, we take on this body and the body has male body, female body, animal body has designed by a by Lord Brahma, the creator of all this. Why has the soul become entrapped like this and playing this different role?

Very nicely Prabhupada has written in the purport, previous purport. As an Amsha, we are all spirit soul. Amsha of Krishna. Just like there is sunlight. Sunlight has come into the room but some minutes back it was in the sun and it has come all the way and traveled here. Isn't it? We understand that. Now can the sun, sunshine, sunlight, is it possible for the sunlight to be independent of the sun? Can sunlight exist without the sun? Not possible at all, isn't it? Constitutionally, it is not possible. The sunlight is an emanation of the sun. In the same way, we are all living entities. We are all conscious entities coming from Krishna. We are all living entities. We are all conscious entities coming from Krishna. We are all conscious entities coming from Krishna. We are all conscious entities coming from Krishna. But, this conscious entities have developed one desire. Sunshine has no desire. It is just light energy. Whereas, we are also energy, Jeeva Shakti of the Lord. And this Jeeva Shakti has developed a desire, I want to be independent of Krishna. I want to be independent of Krishna. I want to be independent of Krishna. I want to be independent of Krishna. Krishna. Just like sunlight has come from sun, we are also Jeeva Shakti coming from Krishna, the Shaktimaan. But the difference is that is a inert, lifeless energy, light energy, heat energy. Whereas we are a Shakti which has got Chetana, consciousness. And this Chetana Shakti, Chit Shakti has developed a desire because it's Chetana. Chetana means has desire, has thinking, feeling. And this Chit Shakti has developed a desire, I must be independent of Krishna.

### illusion, independence, unconstitutional desire
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/D1giBxi2ovc?t=1129
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "This desire of the living entity to be independent of Krishna is called unconstitutional desire."
**Summary:** The speaker elaborates on the unconstitutional desire to be independent of Krishna, comparing it to a dream where sunlight exists without the sun, and explaining that Krishna creates the illusion of the material world to give us the impression of independence.

It is not possible. Sunshine cannot be independent of the sun. It is an emanation of the sun. This desire of the living entity to be independent of Krishna is called unconstitutional desire. It is not constitutional. It is not by our makeup. How we are composed, how we are formed, what are we made of? We are made of Krishna's energy. We have come from Krishna. So we can never sever that. But we have developed a desire. I want to be independent of Krishna. This is possible only in illusion. For example, we can think of sunshine without sun in our dream. We can say last night I had a dream, you know, there was so much sunlight. I looked up at the sky and I didn't see the sun at all. But there was sunshine. Yes, such a thing is possible in illusory dream. Dream will go away. It's a temporary existence in the night. And when we wake up, it's all gone. Right? In the same way, Krishna through Brahma creates an illusion of this world for the living entities to give an impression that we are independent of Krishna.

This is the large population of the society thinks like this. Recognize God. But I have my desires and I should fulfill my desires, my ambitions with God's blessing. But then the reality is that we are a spirit, chetana shakti, coming from Krishna. We rarely think, what is Krishna's plan for me? What does Krishna want me to do? I have come into this world, I am playing different roles. But our spirit of independence is such that I am here, I am independent, I have my independent desires and ambitions. ### Krishna, surrender, relationship

**Summary:** The speaker explains the next level of recognizing God, which involves surrendering to Krishna and aligning our desires with His plan, leading to the understanding of our true relationship with Him, contrasting it with the temporary relationships in the material world.

The next level Krishna teaches in the Bhagavad Gita, in the Vedic literatures, is that, if you are part and parcel of me, Krishna. We are all part and parcel of Krishna. We have come from Krishna. We are an energy of Krishna. What does Krishna want me to do? What is his plan for me? If I am his. If I am his. If I am his. So, this is how Bhagavad Gita ends, by bringing the concept of Sarva-Dharman-Paridhyajya. Ma mekam sharanam vraja. We must surrender to Krishna. We must align our desires, our plans, our activities, with Krishna's activity. And then what happens? Then, Bhagavatam describes further, after sharanagati, after you align, you will come to understand, you have a relation with Krishna. Relation. Relation is a very powerful thing. Just like somebody is a mother, there is a child. The mother is always conscious, I should take care of my child. And child also, playing around a little bit, if some difficulty, some danger comes, mummy, she will run to the mother, and hold on to the mother. That's the meaning of relationship. There is activity. There is feelings. So, now we, next the Vedic literatures inform us, we have a relation with Krishna. What about all these relationships in the material world? This is a drama. It's only a drama relationship. No substance. Just like in the dream also, we sometimes have so many relationships, so many activities. When we wake up in the morning, all the relationship, all the activities has no meaning.

### enjoyment, false ego, Krishna
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/D1giBxi2ovc?t=2466
**Verse References:** BG 9.10, BG 9.11
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Save and accept the Lord, no one can be called the enjoyer, but the living entity falsely desires to become the enjoyer. This is the origin of false ego."
**Summary:** The speaker quotes Srila Prabhupada, emphasizing that Krishna alone is the enjoyer, and the desire to be independent is the origin of false ego, which is a confidential truth revealed in the Bhagavad Gita.

So there is one very nice statement by Srila Prabhupada. Srila Prabhupada, in the previous purport, I'll read that, where is that, oh it's here. Factually, save and accept the Lord, no one can be called the enjoyer. Krishna alone is the enjoyer. Save and accept the Lord, save and accept the Lord, no one can be called the enjoyer, but the living entity falsely desires to become the enjoyer. This is the origin of false ego. This is the origin of ahamkara. This is the important truth Krishna reveals in the 9th chapter of the Bhagavad Gita. In the beginning of the chapter, 9th chapter, Krishna said, idam tu te guhyam pravakshyam anasuyave. Idam tu te guhyam pravakshyam anasuyave. Idam tu te guhyam pravakshyam anasuyave. I am going to tell you the most confidential knowledge. Pravakshyam anasuyave dhyana vigyana sahitam yajnatva mokshase ashubhata. And if you know this truth, you will be freed from all inauspiciousness. What is that truth? Most confidential truth Krishna has revealed in the 9th chapter. There are many aspects of the truth. One of them he is aham hi sarvayagnanam bhogtacha prabhurevaca. This is I am the master, I am the enjoyer of everyone's activities and sacrifices. Natumam abhijananti tatvenathas cavantite. One who don't accept this, I am the master and I am the enjoyer. This is the truth about me. This is the tattva. One who does not accept this. They come to this material world, in this world of illusion. This is the most difficult thing for people to accept. I am not the enjoyer, Krishna is the enjoyer.

---

### spirit soul, body, eternal nature
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/8mdZafj-zZs?t=28
**Verse References:** BG 2.13, BG 2.20
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Krishna teaches that we must understand that there is a body and there is a spirit soul residing in the body."
**Summary:** The speaker explains the fundamental teaching of the Bhagavad Gita: the distinction between the body and the eternal spirit soul, emphasizing the soul's permanence even after the body's death.

But everyone should have a spiritual purpose because we must understand our composition in our present situation. This is the first teaching of the Bhagavad Gita. Krishna teaches that we must understand that there is a body and there is a spirit soul residing in the body. The spirit soul is distinct and different from the body. That is why one day this body can have a heart attack or some other kind of a big disease and finally I will die. When I die, my body will be lying there. The body that everybody was relating with will be lying there. But then people will say, oh he is gone. Who has gone? What has gone? The spirit has gone. So, there is a dual situation here. There is the body and there is the spirit soul. Because of the presence of the spirit soul, the body is animated. I can sing, I can speak, I can do work, I can think, I can solve problems. All this I can do because of the presence of the spirit soul. When the soul leaves the body, it's a dead body. It is just carried and set on fire into ashes. Nothing more can be done with it, when the soul has left the body. But the soul, Krishna teaches, is eternal: na jayate namriyate vā kadācin na hanyate hanyamāne śarīre. And so, we must realize that this body is just an external, temporary covering for the soul. And what happens is, we don't understand these things.

We can run our lives on multiple tracks. All people do that. People run, they have their professional life, they have their personal life, and they have some hobbies, some music, something they'll be practicing, cultivating. They have that and another track. So, life runs on multiple tracks. And we must have one track called spiritual development track. And we may do many other things. Our professional life, personal life. Along with this, we should fire another track in our lives called the spiritual understanding and spiritual development track. ## Doubtless Understanding of Krishna | HG Chanchalapathi Dasa | SB 5 .1.4 | 21.06.2024
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### Krishna consciousness, Grihavrata, Doubt
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/8E1xQmrJR0M?t=60
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "A Grihavrata, one who has taken a vow to execute family duties, has no chance to become Krishna conscious."
**Summary:** King Pariksit's doubt is introduced: how can someone attached to family become perfectly Krishna conscious, given Prahlada Maharaj's statement about Grihavratas?

King Pariksit wondered how a person so attached to wife, children, and home could become so perfectly Krishna conscious. Prahalad Maharaj has said, 'Matirna Krishne Paratasvatova Mithobi Padhyeta Grihavrata Nam.' A Grihavrata, one who has taken a vow to execute family duties, has no chance to become Krishna conscious. This is because most Grihavratas are guided by sense gratification and therefore gradually glide down to the darkest regions of material existence. 'Adanta Ghovir Vishatam Tamisram.' How can they possibly become perfect in Krishna consciousness? Maharaj Pariksit asked Shukadeva Goswami to resolve this great doubt.

### Vedic Literature, Purushottama, Krishna
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/8E1xQmrJR0M?t=1650
**Verse References:** BG 15
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "What does the way all of the Vedic literatures finally boil down to? What is the final statement?"
**Summary:** The speaker introduces verses from the 15th chapter of Bhagavad Gita, where Krishna explains that He is the Purushottama, the supreme person, and that understanding this is the essence of Vedic knowledge.

How carefully Prabhupada has picked up all these things and presented to us in modern context. This is described in the Bhagavad Gita and Bhagavatam. There is one very nice verse, two verses I will read this in the Bhagavad Gita. It's a short chapter, 15th chapter. Krishna concluding, and in the concluding verses, Krishna is actually explaining what does the way all of the Vedic literatures finally boil down to. What is the final statement? It's one of the very very important and interesting verses. Yomam evam asam mudho janati purushottamam Maam janati asam mudho janati Asam mudho janati means doubtlessly know. Know what? Yomam evam asam mudho janati purushottamam I am the purushottamam. There are many purushas. Already Krishna explained there are two kinds of purushas. Some of them, some of the purushas are called kshara purushas. Some of the purushas are called akshara purushas. And kshara purushas are those who are in the material world and akshara purushas are those who are in the spiritual world. There are a few verses before Krishna points that out. Dvavimau purushau loke ksharascha akshara yevacha There are dvavimau purushau loke. There are two kinds of purushas.

---
### Purushottama, Kshara, Akshara
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/8E1xQmrJR0M?t=1774
**Verse References:** BG 15.18-19
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "And I am transcendental to both kshara and akshara purushas."
**Summary:** The speaker elaborates on the concepts of 'kshara' (fallible) and 'akshara' (infallible) purushas, and introduces the 'uttama purusha' (supreme person), who is transcendental to both and maintains the universes.

Ksharaha sarvabhuthani kutastho akshara ucyate Kutastha means situated in the spiritual world. Kutastha. Kutastha means fixed up. Only in the spiritual world you will be fixed up. In the material world you will not be fixed up, you will be vacillating. One idea, one concept, another concept, different pursuits we will be doing. Only when we are in the spiritual world, kutastha akshara ucyate. So he said that there are two kinds of purushas. But then uttama purushastva anyaha There is one more third purusha who is anya, different from these kshara and akshara purushas and he is uttama purusha. And that purusha is paramatmeti udakhrataha. He is the paramatma. He is celebrated as paramatma. lokatrayam avishya He enters the three worlds. vibhrithyavyayaishvaraha vibhrithi He maintains the three universes. All the universes. and yasmat ksharamatitoham aksharadapichottamaha And I am transcendental to both kshara and akshara purushas. Athosmi loke vedhecha pratithah purushottamaha And hence I am celebrated in the Vedic literatures and in the society as the purushottama.

### Krishna, Purushottama, Knowledge
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/8E1xQmrJR0M?t=1948
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy

So, this is krishnamatihi. Because Krishna is purushottama, and one who is convinced about it, that Krishna is the purushottama, and he renders such devotional service, bhajati maam sarvabhavena bharata So, that doubtless understanding that Krishna is the purushottama, and we must render service to him, sa sarvavit How is this knowing everything? Just like you see in a prison, there may be prisoners, and among prisoners, all kinds of prisoners will be there, a person who has understood that, yes, why I have landed in the prison, and I must get out of the prison, by becoming a law-abiding citizen, he has understood the right thing, we will say.

### Material World, Reformation, Knowledge
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/8E1xQmrJR0M?t=2012
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "He has really served the purpose of the prison, he has understood the purpose of the prison, he has understood everything."
**Summary:** The speaker continues the prison analogy, contrasting the prisoner who simply performs tasks within the prison with the one who understands the purpose of the prison as an opportunity for reformation and understanding one's relationship with the Supreme.

In prison, there may be some, there may be one electrician who got, landed in the prison, and they will use him in the prison, you fix this bulb, fix this wire, and he will be doing that. So, somebody may say, oh, he is such a good electrician, you know, in our prison, he can fix all problems of electric problems, all those, good. Someone may be a cook, someone may be something else, all kinds of prisoners are there, but among all of them, one who has understood that, I made a mistake, I should become law-abiding, he has really served the purpose of the prison, he has understood the purpose of the prison, he has understood everything, and he is now. In the same way, in the material world, we may find many intelligent people, there are scientists, there are economists, there are so many people, they know so many things, they are like the electrician, cook and tailor, they know so many things of this world, they have not understood everything, why this world is there, why the material world is there, it's an opportunity for reformation, to understand our relation with the supreme.

## Everything is Connected to Narayana in Loving Service | @ChanchalapathiDas
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### devotion, Narayana, purpose
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/L-vx4MHi0T8?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Everything is related to Vasudeva, Narayana."
**Summary:** The speaker explains that just as businesses focus on pleasing customers, everything, according to the Vedas, is focused on and meant for Narayana, and without that connection, it lacks meaning or value.

Just like in business they say, we are very customer focused. That means they are saying, we are customer para. We want to please our customers. We want to satisfy our customers. We want to delight our customers. Like this, right? This is how management works. Brahma is saying, Vedas are Narayana para. Loka, focused on Narayana. Lokas are meant for Narayana. Makaha, the sacrifices are meant for Narayana. Everything is related to Vasudeva, Narayana. Without that, it has no meaning or value.

## Harness Body and Mind Spiritually | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa | ISKCON Bangalore Sanga
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### mind control, self-control, spiritual practice
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/U6B5gqgV8aQ?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "As spiritualists, we do not trust our mind."
**Summary:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa explains that spiritualists must understand the forces within the body, especially the mind, and not surrender to its dictates, emphasizing that intelligence and the soul are higher than the mind.

Prabhupada explains that a spiritualist has to be very sober, introspective, thoughtful, grave. Vacho vegam, manasa, krodha vegam, jihva vegam, udhara upastha vegam. It means a kind of a force in the body. Prabhupada gives the example, just like our body is designed in such a way, when there is a nature's call, it creates a force, irresistible force. We all have to rush to the washroom. In the same way, there are other forces in this body and one of them is the force of the mind. As spiritualists, we must know these workings of the mind, workings of the forces in this body, so that we know how to deal with them. Shukadev Goswami is giving one such example. He is saying, this mind which is unsteady and which comes with a force, don't trust this mind. This is the first instruction. So, Prabhupada explains, as spiritualists, we do not trust our mind. Means, we do not surrender to the dictations of our mind. The mind comes with a force. Mind comes with an idea. Let's do this. Let's do that. You do this. You do that. And it comes with a certain force. Don't trust your mind. This is the instruction. Watch the mind's action. In other words, intelligence is higher than the mind. Soul is higher than the intelligence. And we are that soul.

---

## How to Become Prideless? | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### humility, spiritual development, devotion
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/IyGx5N8hp2Q?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "If we make an attempt to become prideless on a mental plane, there is a chance that we will become proud of pridelessness."
**Summary:** The speaker discusses the paradox of becoming proud of pridelessness and emphasizes that genuine spiritual qualities arise from devotion to Krishna and attaining a spiritual platform, rather than directly trying to acquire them.

Some time back, one devotee asked me, what if a devotee becomes proud of pridelessness? Yes, it happens. It can happen. We can become proud of many other virtues that a devotee is supposed to have. But, our method of developing all these qualities is not by trying to acquire those qualities separately. We first become devotees of Krishna. To become genuine devotees of Krishna, we have to come to a spiritual platform. Our principle is, in such a person's heart, all divine qualities will come about. If we make an attempt to become prideless on a mental plane, there is a chance that we will become proud of pridelessness. But our attempt is to come to a spiritual platform. And when one comes to a genuine, spiritual platform, we will develop genuine spiritual qualities.

---

### Paul's erratic behavior, Screaming and shouting, Realization of danger, Leaving the loft
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/irID2uAh7lY?t=867
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers

## Importance of Following the Guru Strictly | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa | SB 5.1.5 | 16.08.2024
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### devotional service, obstacles, Vaishnava Aparadha
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/i5ImCRHRxU8?t=126
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Similarly, the power of Vaishnava Aparadha is so great that even an advanced devotee becomes almost devoid of his spiritual assets if he commits it."
**Summary:** This segment discusses impediments to devotional service, focusing on Vaishnava Aparadha and the desire of the Lord, while emphasizing that Krishna consciousness is eternal and cannot be lost.

Who has once absorbed his mind in the glories of the Supreme Personality of Godhead may sometimes be influenced by impediments, but he still does not give up his exalted devotional position. According to Srila Vishwanath Chakravarthy Thakura, there are two kinds of impediments to devotional service. The first is an offense at the lotus feet of a Vaishnava. This is called Vaishnava Aparadha. Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu warned His devotees not to commit Vaishnava Aparadha, which He described as the mad elephant offense. When a mad elephant enters a beautiful garden, it destroys everything, leaving a barren field. Similarly, the power of Vaishnava Aparadha is so great that even an advanced devotee becomes almost devoid of his spiritual assets if he commits it. Since Krishna consciousness is eternal, it cannot be destroyed altogether, but advancement may be checked for the time being. Thus, Vaishnava Aparadha is one kind of impediment to devotional service. Sometimes, however, the Supreme Personality of Godhead or His devotee desires to impede one's devotional service. For example, Hiranyakashyapu and Hiranyakshya were formerly Jaya and Vijaya, the gatekeepers in Vaikuntha, but by the desire of the Lord, they became His enemies for three lives. Thus, the desire of the Lord is another kind of impediment. But in both cases, the pure devotee once advanced in Krishna consciousness cannot be lost. Following the orders of his superiors, Swayambhuva and Lord Brahma, Priyavrata accepted family life, but this did not mean he lost his position in devotional service. Krishna consciousness is perfect and eternal, and therefore it cannot be lost under any circumstances. Because the material world is full of obstructions to advancement in Krishna consciousness, there may appear to be many impediments, yet Krishna, the Supreme Personality of Godhead, declares in Bhagavad Gita, 9.31, once one has taken shelter at the lotus feet of the Lord, he cannot be lost. 

---
### devotional service, karma, material attachment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/i5ImCRHRxU8?t=310
**Verse References:** BG 6.43, BG 7.28
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The fact is, however, that one becomes a devotee when he is completely freed from all reactions to sinful life."
**Summary:** This segment continues to discuss the eternal nature of Krishna consciousness, citing examples of devotees who appear to fall but are ultimately protected, and addresses the apparent contradiction between material attachment and devotional advancement, setting up the context for the chapter on Priyavrata's life.

In this verse, the word Shivatamam is very significant. Shivatamam means the most auspicious. The devotional path is so auspicious that a devotee cannot be lost under any circumstances. This is described in the Srimad Bhagavad Gita by the Lord Himself. Parthnaivehanamutra Vinashastasya Vidyavrata. My dear Arjuna, for a devotee, there is no question of being lost, either in this life or in the next. In Bhagavad Gita, 6.43, the Lord clearly explains how this is so. Tatratam buddhi samyogam labhate pavarvadehikam yadate chatato bhuyaha samsiddho kuru nandana. By the order of the Lord, a perfect devotee sometimes comes to this material world like an ordinary human being. Because of his previous practice, such a perfect devotee naturally becomes a devotee. He becomes attached to devotional service, apparently without cause. Despite all kinds of impediments due to surrounding circumstances, he automatically perseveres in devotional service and gradually advances until he once again becomes perfect. Below Mangal Thakura had been an advanced devotee in his previous life, but in his next life he became greatly fallen and was attached to a prostitute. Suddenly, however, his entire behavior was changed by the words of the very prostitute, who had so much attracted him, and he became a great devotee. In the lives of exalted devotees, there are many such instances, proving that once one has taken to the shelter of the lotus feet of the Lord, he cannot be lost. Kaunteya pratijanihi namey bhaktav pranashyati. The fact is, however, that one becomes a devotee when he is completely freed from all reactions to sinful life. As Krishna states in Bhagavad Gita, 7.28, Esham tuantagatam paapam jananam punyakam te dvandhva moha nirmukta bhajan teman dhrdha vrataah. Persons who have acted piously in previous lives and in this life, whose sinful actions are completely eradicated and who are freed from the duality of illusion, engage themselves in my service with determination. On the other hand, as Prahlad Maharaj said, Matirna krishne paratas svatova mito bhipadyeta grihavrataana. A person who is too attached to materialistic things, family life, home, family, wife, children and so on, cannot develop Krishna consciousness. These apparent contradictions are resolved in the life of a devotee by the grace of the Supreme Lord and therefore a devotee is never bereft of his position on the path of liberation which is described in this verse as Shiva tamam padavim Dasan dhristavak chidantaprabhat. So in this chapter of the Srimad Bhagavatam entitled The Activities of Maharaj Priyavrata we just saw Parikshit Maharaj asking different questions about Priyavrata's life, how he was a great devotee, renounced from all material activities, but then he took up, he became a grihasta, became a householder, had two wives, had many children and apparently became attached to family members and he was a ruler, he was a king dealing with all the complications of a king's life. How did this happen? Because if somebody is attached to family life and such materialistic things, he cannot develop Krishna consciousness and if one has become advanced in Krishna consciousness, he will not become attached to material things, so this looks like Priyavrata's life seems to be a contradiction, so that was the question that Parikshit Maharaj has raised.

---

### Lord's desires, personality of Godhead, enjoyment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/i5ImCRHRxU8?t=1089
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The absolute truth is a personality. And what is the meaning of personality? Personality means somebody who has got desires."
**Summary:** This segment explains the Lord's desire to impede devotional service as a manifestation of His personality and desire for variegated enjoyment, using the example of Jaya and Vijaya becoming demons to fight with the Lord.

Actually, a conscious person, a very primary characteristic of a conscious person, personality is having desires for enjoyment. That's why ultimately Kama Deva means Krishna. Because Kama, desire to enjoy, ultimately belongs to the Lord. He is the ultimate Kama Deva. So He is the Supreme Personality, means He has desires to enjoy. And enjoyment is not one-sided, it is variegated, it is multi-dimensional. And so, Lord, sometimes everyone is praising me. Okay, let me, somebody should also fight with me. That's another nice thing. So the Lord may decide, okay, my dear two devotees, I will impede your devotional service here. You can do another kind of devotional service by going there and taking birth as Asuras. And I will come and fight. And you should be strong. Don't worry. It is a tough fight. Otherwise, what is the use? I come and fight and then suddenly you surrender. It doesn't please me. So I want you to become powerful demons. Shake the whole universe. Then I will come. Then we will have fight. You see how this is? This is actually, Bhagavatam is establishing the personality. The absolute truth is a personality. And what is the meaning of personality? Personality means somebody who has got desires. And he pursues those desires for enjoyment. And the pursuit of the desire for enjoyment constitutes activities. That is actually the Lord and His associates.

### material world, spiritual world, perspective
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/i5ImCRHRxU8?t=1220
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "The greater reality and the dominant reality is the spiritual world. The material world is a small portion."
**Summary:** This segment uses the analogy of a prisoner's limited view of the world to illustrate how our material perspective obscures the greater reality of the spiritual world and the Lord's pastimes.

That's actually the truth. What happens is, our view of the world and the creation, it is just like the prisoner's view in a prison in our world. The prisoner is in the prison. He is used to things in the prison. Big walls. He is conditioned. He cannot escape. He cannot relate with the family members. It's all restricted. He wants to enjoy. It's all restricted. So this is actually the perspective of a prisoner. In the same way, our perspective is actually we see from the material world. Actually the truth is, we all know, we all are outside the prison in this world. So we know that how the world is full of irrigatedness. So many activities. There are parks. There are malls. There are restaurants. So many ways to enjoy. By the way, there is one small portion in our city, in every city, called the prison. In the same way, the reality is, the greater reality is, the Lord and His associates and the wonderful pastimes that happen in the spiritual domain. By the way, there is one part of the creation called the material world where all the rebellious living entities are put there. So, this is actually the reality. But, because we are in the material world, we are trying to understand the spiritual reality from the material domain. It's just like the prisoners looking at, oh, there is something called a free world, is it? Oh, there is some park. There are parks there. There are all such beautiful things. Okay, maybe there. So, that's the view of an inmate of a prison. Actually, that's the way we look at when we hear about the spiritual world. But, the greater reality and the dominant reality is the spiritual world. The material world is a small portion.

### Lord's desires, devotee's role, Krishna consciousness
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/i5ImCRHRxU8?t=1350
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Krishna consciousness is perfect and it is eternal and it cannot be lost under any circumstance."
**Summary:** This segment reiterates the Lord's personality and desires, emphasizing that devotees take on different roles to provide Him with various forms of pleasure, and uses Priyavrata as an example of how devotional service is not lost even when following the orders of superiors in seemingly contradictory activities.

So, so this is the, so these are the reasons why certain times the Lord wants, Lord is a personality and He has got desires and He wants to pursue those desires for His pleasure and His own devotees take up different roles to give Him different varieties of pleasure and that is another example. So, this is an example Prabhupada has quoted of Jaya and Vijaya where their devotional service was in one sense impeded but actually not in another sense. It was meant for a larger, another kind of a pleasure of the Lord. So, sometimes we may see this kind of an impediment. Another one is Priyavrata himself. Priyavrata was not, his impediment came not from the Lord but from his devotee. Swayambhuva Manu and Brahma, both great personalities, great devotees, they went and told Priyavrata who was in his, like it is described here, Makaranda Rasa, Aveshita Cheta Saha, he was absorbed in transcendental mellows of the Lord but they went and told him, no, no, now you come, become a king, become a householder, have queens, have children, all of that. So, he may do that but Priyavrata when he is doing that, he never lost his shivatamam padaveena prayena hinvanti. They never lose their spiritual position. That is to be appreciated and understood because Krishna consciousness is perfect and it is eternal and it cannot be lost under any circumstance.

### following orders, superior's instructions, devotional service
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/i5ImCRHRxU8?t=1473
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Bhakti is such that if one is in different kinds of roles, if one is in different kinds of situations, but those roles and situations are under the order of the superiors, then one will not lose his devotional position."
**Summary:** This segment highlights the importance of following the orders of superiors, using Priyavrata's acceptance of family life as an example, and suggests that Srila Prabhupada's life exemplifies this principle, potentially warranting inclusion in future iterations of the Bhagavatam.

So here, important point is following the orders of his superiors Swayambhuva Manu and Lord Brahma, Priyavrata accepted family life but this did not mean he lost his position in devotional service. This is the point that this chapter is going to point out. Bhakti is such that if one is in different kinds of roles, if one is in different kinds of situations, but those roles and situations are under the order of the superiors, then one will not lose his devotional position. This is the crux of the matter. shivatamam padaveena prayena hinvanti One will not lose his devotional position if one is under the order of superiors one is acting in this way. And this principle and many other principles of the Bhagavatam they were actually demonstrated in the life of Srila Prabhupada. I heard somewhere one devotee describing actually Prabhupada's life is so exemplary. It's not unlikely Vyasadeva will include Prabhupada's life in some part of the Bhagavatam which he composes in some other part of the universe. Because lives of devotees demonstrate spiritual principles and Prabhupada's life is a great demonstration of one of the important principles which is to follow the orders of the superior. Prabhupada's life was fully a manifestation of the following the order of his spiritual master.

## Lecture on Panihati festival | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa | 20.06.2024
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### Paanihati Festival, Krishna Consciousness, Guru
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/0wGOBQXAnLk?t=15
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Guru is someone who gives Krishna to the forgetful living entities."
**Summary:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa introduces the Paanihati Festival, explaining its significance in Gaudiya Sampradaya and its connection to revealing Krishna through Balaram and the Guru.

So today we are observing a very unique festival, unique to our Gaudiya Sampradaya. Followers of Chaitanya Mahaprabhu observe this festival. This festival is known as Paani Hati Festival because originally it happened in a small village called Paani Hati. This festival is also called Danda Mahotsav. Danda means a punishment, a festival of punishment. Contradictory. How can the festival which is joyous be a punishment? How can punishment which is miserable be a festival? So we will see all of that in a short while. Also this festival conveys a very profound spiritual message. Krishna says, "I am not revealed to everyone." There is a curtain of Yogamaya that is covering me. So Krishna, who is the supreme personality of God, who is the Param Sathya, Who is the Param Tattva. And in this material world, all the living entities are in a spirit of independence from the Lord. Don't want to surrender to the Lord, want to lead a life independent of the Lord. To them the Lord is not revealed easily. Krishna Baheermukha Jeeva. Our position in this material world is Krishna Baheermukha Jeeva. We are Jeeva, but we are Baheermukha, turned away from Krishna. But this is not a natural situation. Just like the sunshine cannot hope to be independent of the sun. Can sunshine ever be independent of the sun? So the living entities who are here in the material world who have turned away from Krishna, how will they ever be rectified from their illusory imagined position of being independent of the Lord? So Lord has one immediate expansion tattva called prakasha tattva. The Lord's prakasha tattva's function is to prakasha, to make, to illuminate, to reveal the truth to the living entities, to the living entities who are in ignorance. We are in such an ignorance just like the sunshine thinking I will be independent of the sun. Most ridiculous, most impossible, that is our situation. To such ignorant living entities to bring prakasha, to illuminate them, there is a expansion of the Lord, and that expansion of the Lord is Balaram. So Krishna is the original person, and Balaram is his immediate expansion, and he is prakasha tattva. Krishna is para tattva or bhagavat tattva, non different. Krishna and Balaram, Krishna and Balaram, both are on the same spiritual absolute position, but Balaram is the one who reveals Krishna, and one who reveals to the living entities about all this is guru, and that guru is actually a representation of Balaram prakasha tattva. This is the understanding the guru is someone who reveals Krishna. Guru is someone who gives Krishna to the forgetful living entities.

---
### Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, Nithyananda Prabhu, Preaching
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/0wGOBQXAnLk?t=463
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Even we can please Nithyananda Prabhu by preaching Krishna consciousness."
**Summary:** The speaker explains that when Krishna came as Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, Balaram came as Nithyananda Prabhu, and just as guru reveals Krishna, Balaram reveals Krishna, Nithyananda Prabhu reveals Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, emphasizing the importance of preaching Krishna consciousness to please Nithyananda Prabhu.

So when Krishna came as Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, Balaram, the prakasha tattva of the Lord, came as Nithyananda Prabhu. Just as guru reveals Krishna, Balaram reveals Krishna, Nithyananda Prabhu reveals Chaitanya Mahaprabhu. One of the important leelas of Nithyananda Prabhu in Navadvip, he shows how to understand Krishna, how to please Krishna, and one of the important leelas of Nithyananda Prabhu was to go around and preach to the town folks of Navadvip, and all kinds of people including Jagai and Madai. He wanted to give Krishna, he wanted to give Chaitanya Mahaprabhu to everyone. That is the way even we can please Nithyananda Prabhu by preaching Krishna consciousness.

### Raghunath Das Goswami, Nithyananda Prabhu, Paanihati Festival
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/0wGOBQXAnLk?t=541
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Punishment from the Lord is very desirable because it's a form of mercy of the master."
**Summary:** The lecture narrates the story of Raghunath Das Goswami, his desire to serve Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, and his encounter with Nithyananda Prabhu in Panihati, where he was 'punished' by being asked to feed all of Nithyananda Prabhu's associates with Chida-dahi, highlighting the significance of this event in the Paanihati festival.

Now in Chaitanya Leela, there is the great devotee Raghunath Das Goswami. Before he became a Goswami, before he came to that state, he was born into a very rich family in a place called Saptagram, and from a very young age he had the great opportunity to see Chaitanya Mahaprabhu when he had just taken sanyas, when Chaitanya Mahaprabhu had taken sanyas, and he had a strong desire to come to Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, and he was making an attempt to come to Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, but his family members, father, mother, would not allow him. They thought that no our son, because they came from a rich family, they thought their son, our son should be like us, he should inherit all our property, he should inherit the position that we have, and he should be a normal worldly person, but he did not have any interest in the material activities. He wanted to be with Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, serve the mission of Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, and so he would try to run away from home as a young boy, young man, and his father would send his guards and bring him back. So this happened many many times, and every time Raghunath Das's father would bring him back. So Raghunath was very unhappy, he was longing to be with Chaitanya Mahaprabhu to serve his mission, be in his association. So around that time near Saptagram, there is a small village Panihatti. Nithyananda Prabhu had come with a lot of his associates. Nithyananda Prabhu would be travelling around in Bengal broadcasting Krishna consciousness on the order of Chaitanya Mahaprabhu. So he came there, and he would do kirtans, he would tell about Krishna to people, and he had hundreds of associates with him or thousands of associates with him. So Raghunath Das when he heard that Nithyananda Prabhu has come to a neighboring village, he came to see him, and from a distance out of humility, from a distance he was offering his respects, but Chaitanya Mahaprabhu's associates, sorry Nithyananda Prabhu's associates pointed out Raghunath Das is there far away. So Nithyananda Prabhu wanted to bring him, so they sent message and Raghunath Das was brought. Nithyananda Prabhu was also, he had a sense of a very unique sense of humor, and so when Raghunath Das was brought close to him, Nithyananda Prabhu said, "Raghunath you are trying to hide from me." And Raghunath said no no Prabhu, not at all. And then he said, "I want to punish you today." Raghunath Das was very happy. Nithyananda Prabhu is going to punish me. So punishment from the Lord is very, from the master is very desirable because it's a form of mercy of the master. So Nithyananda Prabhu said the punishment is, "I know you are coming from a very rich family, you feed all my associates, and I have a special request, you should make cheetah dahi, flat rice mixed with yogurt flat rice mixed with condensed milk, and two parts like this, you should distribute to everybody." So Raghunath Das was very happy to accept this punishment. He had all the resources, so he brought all his assistants from his home and got purchased a lot of cheetah dahi, mixed mangoes to it mixed bananas to it. Chaitanya Charitamruta says he mixed bananas and honey to all of this and served Nithyananda Prabhu and all the associates on the banks of Ganga, and at that time Nithyananda Prabhu made a statement, "We belong to the cowherd clan, and coming on a picnic like this on the bank of a river and having delicious food to eat is something that we love." Actually this statement is significant because Nithyananda Prabhu is Balarama and Krishna and Balarama and the cowherd boys would go on the banks of Yamuna and they would have their picnic everyday all the things that their mothers had brought had sent with them, they would share called Vanabhoj. So that's what Nithyananda Prabhu was reminiscing.

---
### Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, Nithyananda Prabhu, Mercy, Detachment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/0wGOBQXAnLk?t=893
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "If we get the mercy of Nithyananda Prabhu, all our samsaravasana, all our material desires which keeps us in this material world will go away."
**Summary:** The speaker concludes by describing how Nithyananda Prabhu brought Chaitanya Mahaprabhu to the festival, emphasizing the importance of receiving the mercy of Nithyananda Prabhu to attain the lotus feet of Chaitanya Mahaprabhu and to be freed from material desires, ending with prayers and glorifications.

And at that time Nithyananda Prabhu by his meditation brought Chaitanya Mahaprabhu there, and only a few fortunate souls it is said could see Chaitanya and Nithyananda, and there was ecstatic uproarious kirtan with Chaitanya and Nithyananda and chanting of the holy names which filled the air, and this Chiradahi which was given to Nithyananda and Chaitanya Mahaprabhu was served to everyone. So this was a festival and then towards the end of the festival mystically Chaitanya Mahaprabhu vanished from the scene and only Nithyananda Prabhu and other associates were there, and the next day Nithyananda Prabhu was moving away from there to another place and Raghunath Das once again came and requested him that my situation is I am not able to my parents are holding me back I want to be serving Chaitanya Mahaprabhu and now at that time Nithyananda Prabhu placed his lotus feet on the head of Raghunath Das who was lying fallen down at his feet and then Nithyananda Prabhu said very soon you will be freed from all the obstacles and exactly like that in a few next few days or weeks Raghunath Das was able to go and be with Chaitanya Mahaprabhu. So if we have to attain the lotus feet of Chaitanya Mahaprabhu service to Chaitanya Mahaprabhu we should get the blessings of Nithyananda Prabhu who is the Prakasha Tattva. So Raghunath Das received the mercy of Nithyananda Prabhu to receive the mercy of Nithyananda Prabhu we have to please him. Raghunath Das pleased Nithyananda Prabhu by fulfilling his request to have a big festival of Chitadahi. So this is the principle that we need the mercy of Nithyananda Prabhu to get Chaitanya Mahaprabhu we need the mercy of Balaram to attain Krishna's lotus feet and Krishna's service and hence this festival commemorates this important spiritual principle and so in our temple here on the banks of Kalyani we offer Chitadahi to Chaitanya and Nithyananda Prabhu and they will go around in a nauka vihar and all of us will also receive the prasadam of Chitadahi remembering this past time let us pray to Nithyananda Prabhu by Nithyananda Prabhu's mercy aarkabe nithai chander karunahave samsaravasana morekabe tuchahave if we get the mercy of Nithyananda Prabhu all our samsaravasana all our material desires which keeps us in this material world will go away. So this is a special festival where we pray to Nithyananda Prabhu to shower his mercy so that all our material desires will go away and we become qualified to go back to the spiritual world with these few reflections we will next proceed to the next part of the festival Shri Nithyananda Prabhu ki Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu ki Shri Raghunath Das Goswami ki Shri Chaitanya Mahaprabhu ki Shri Raghunath Das Goswami ki Srila Prabhupada who revealed all these things to us Srila Prabhupada ki Nithyananda Prabhu ki.

## Q & A on Theory of Everything - The Vedanta Perspective (Part 1)
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### science, illusion, limitations of science
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/9p0dGnuA05M?t=95
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Science works well in a certain domain, the domain of the material universe and if you have to investigate things, phenomena outside of this domain, simply the tools of science break down."
**Summary:** The speaker discusses how modern science presents itself as an authority on the universe and how to see through this illusion, explaining that science has limitations and works well only in the material domain.

The first question is, how to get rid of being carried away by the power of seeing through the wheel of illusion created by modern materialistic science, by which it presents itself as the authority on the universe? Okay, let's read this a little bit slowly. We don't want to get carried away. How to get rid of being carried away by the power of seeing, power of seeing through the wheel of illusion, okay, to see that there is an illusion created by modern materialistic science by which it presents itself as the authority on the universe. Okay. Modern science presents itself as an authority on the universe. And how do we see through this illusion and how do we see things correctly? Okay. As I was explaining earlier, science and technology working together has created that kind of an immense confidence and trust in people that science and technology is the most credible source of knowledge in the world today. So, that's exactly what has happened. Science develops to some extent and then the technology takes over, uses some of those principles and creates things in our life which improves our life and then we start having tremendous faith in science because from science technology has come, from technology our life has improved. We see that link. But if you ask some very serious scientists in the world, they also admit that science has its limitations. Science works well in a certain domain, the domain of the material universe and if you have to investigate things, phenomena outside of this domain, simply the tools of science break down.

### science, ethics, morality
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/9p0dGnuA05M?t=274
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Although this is a very scientific solution, it is not a scientific solution. It is not a scientific answer. Practically, no one will be ready to implement this."
**Summary:** The speaker shares an example from Professor Charles Townes about the limitations of science when dealing with morality and ethics.

I have given one popular example, I don't know if you have all heard. This is an example given by Professor Charles Townes. Professor Charles Townes was the inventor of the laser beam, somewhere in the 1960s and he got a Nobel Prize for physics for his work on lasers. He is a very devout Christian and he has, he made a statement and he gives an example. Suppose there is a country, a country made a statement. I have a very simple example. Let's say there is a country with 1000 people. That's the population of the country. And in that country, they have enough resources to provide good life, housing, health care, roads, jobs, all of this for only 900 people. But there are 1000 people in the country. And because of that, extra hundred people, the resources, there is a crunch and there is a certain level of poverty. People are not able to have as much as they would want to have. And there is a certain want. Now, if you were to ask, look for a scientific solution for this, a very simple, straightforward solution will be, out of that country of one thousand people, you eliminate hundred people, then you will have nine hundred people in the country and you will have enough resources so that everyone can have good life. Although this is a very scientific solution, it is not a scientific solution. It is not a scientific answer. Practically, no one will be ready to implement this. There will be so many more complex questions that come up. On what basis shall we decide these hundred people will be eliminated? And do we have, there are many moral and ethical questions that come into play. In other words, Professor Charles Townes is saying that there are certain questions, certain aspects of morality, ethics, and all of those kind of things, which are actually today outside the domain of science.

### science, fine tuning, universe
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/9p0dGnuA05M?t=477
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "This has serious religious consequences."
**Summary:** The speaker discusses the fine tuning of the universe and how even slight variations in constants would prevent the universe from existing as it does.

There is one phenomenon in physics, in science, and I would like to quote Stephen Hawking's comment on that. This understanding is called fine tuning of the universe. There are a few constants in science. For example, the speed of light, the charge of an electron, the mass of an electron, gravitational constant. And there are about 15, 20 or 25 constants like that. These are considered to be very important constants in physics. And these constants are the way they are. Like for instance, the charge of an electron or the mass of an electron or the speed of light. Now, there are a lot of scientists who have worked on this and they have, in fact, even Stephen Hawking had worked on this. And they have found that if any of these constants were even slightly different by a billion billion, that is 10 power minus 18, if it was a little different, the world would not have come about like this. The world would not have come about the way it is. And we would not have had the galaxies and the solar systems. And we would not be sitting like this today and asking questions and thinking about our own existence. So all of this has happened because those constants were fine tuned. They were not a little bit this way or that way. Now, how did this fine tuning of the universe happen? When this discussion was happening, one of the comments that Stephen Hawking made was that this has serious religious consequences. So it's a fact that the universe that we live in has come about even according to science and has certain constants. And if these constants were even slightly different, we would not have the universe that we have.

### science, big bang, universe
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/9p0dGnuA05M?t=882
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Actually, it is simply a mathematical equation at t equal to zero becoming a singularity, having no solutions. And that's known as the big bang."
**Summary:** The speaker explains the Big Bang theory, clarifying that it represents a mathematical singularity where equations have no solutions.

And according to science, the whole universe began with a big bang. Right? So the thought came to my mind. Where did this big bang occur? And if we were to know that place, that point, that would be the universe Uttri. Right? That's the place where the universe began. The whole universe should go there too, because that's the holy pilgrimage of the whole for the whole universe, because that's where the universe began. So this thought came to my mind. And then afterwards I was just reflecting on it. And then I did some reading. Actually, it's very interesting. Where is the point that the big bang occurred? In fact, there is no point in the universe where the big bang occurred because there was no point in space. Space itself did not exist. It is from the big bang space occurred. Space, time, energy, matter, everything came from that big bang. Then I was doing some more reading. And then I found that actually what scientists mean by a big bang is when they have tried to create mathematical models for all these things. And they come up with an equation. And that equation at t greater than zero has meaningful significance. And you get to explain how the universe is evolving. But when you put t equal to zero, you don't have a solution for that equation. You come to a mathematical situation, what is known as singularity. You can't solve the equation. There are no known solutions for that equation. When t equal to zero, when that equation cannot give results, that is known as the big bang. Actually, scientists are very good in giving good names. They give fancy names. And they are, you know, creative people and intelligent people. They give good names. And the common people pick up from that. And we get the impression that, you know, big bang theory means it's a big bang occurred. And then we get the feeling that it's like some kind of an explosion, some like a firework, Diwali fireworks or something happening in the universe. And then the universe came about. Actually, it is simply a mathematical equation at t equal to zero becoming a singularity, having no solutions. And that's known as the big bang.

So if you see, if you talk to real serious scientists, they all admit that there are many, many, many things that we don't know. So it is a fact that science, although has works very well in a certain domain and provides very meaningful explanations, which is used by technology to improve things in our life. But at the really, if you go into the very basics of things, science has many things which are not clearly understood. So if we know some of these things, I think we will understand that, yes, science is doing well, but in a certain domain. But there are so many other aspects. A true scientist will admit that we don't know how these things work. Like, for example, in the realm of consciousness, how consciousness works. What is conscious? How come? How consciousness comes about? These are all very difficult questions, even in science. So a veil of illusion that science can provide everything, it's not actually, it is an illusion that we have created.

### vedanta, srimad bhagavatam, kali yuga
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/9p0dGnuA05M?t=1390
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "For the sake of people of Kali Yuga, for their better comprehension, for their better understanding, that Vedanta had to be expanded in the form of the Srimad Bhagavatam."
**Summary:** The speaker explains why the Vedanta Sutra was expanded into the Srimad Bhagavatam, emphasizing the need for easier accessibility and understanding in Kali Yuga.

All the Vedic knowledge was compressed in the form of Vedanta Sutra. So what was the need for again expanding it in the form of Srimad Bhagavatam? Yes. We discussed about how the history of Vedic knowledge, the Vedic knowledge, was compressed, not the Vedic knowledge. The last word of Vedic knowledge. The last, the ultimate of Vedic wisdom, Vedanta, was compressed in the form of Sutras, so that people can carry that in their memory and recollect them and expand on that. Now, what was the need for again expanding it in the form of Srimad Bhagavatam? One reason is, Veda Vyasa and the other sages foresaw that in Kali Yuga, this vast Vedic knowledge and then coming to the Vedanta knowledge and then being able to comprehend and understand the Vedanta knowledge is not an easy thing. First of all, in previous Yugas, life was long. And so you can afford to take a slow process of evolution and understanding. But in Kali Yuga, the life is very short. It's just 100 years. Like Prahalad Maharaj analyzes in the Bhagavatam. And first 15 years goes away in playful activities. And then some more years of sleeping. 50% of the life is spent sleeping. And then we have to earn money, maintain our family and all of that. Finally, how much time is available for us to actually introspect and understand spiritual matters? And even at that time, human life in Kali Yuga is going to be full of disturbances. You see how for just basic living, people have to work so hard in Kali Yuga. And they are very disturbed because of the kind of lifestyle that we have. So realizing that, the sages wanted Vedanta once again to be expanded and made more easily accessible, understandable and hence they wanted the Srimad Bhagavatam to come about. And it was the will of the Lord. The Lord inspired Vyasadeva to do this. And hence, Vedanta Sutra, although it was compressed for the sake of people of Kali Yuga, for their better comprehension, for their better understanding, that Vedanta had to be expanded in the form of the Srimad Bhagavatam.

### karma, destiny, effort
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/9p0dGnuA05M?t=1671
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "We have to do our cheshta, our effort is also an important factor. And there is no need to over endeavor because what we are due to get is already destined."
**Summary:** The speaker addresses the concept of destiny and effort, emphasizing the importance of fulfilling one's duty without overexerting, using the analogy of the lion who must still hunt.

where you need to reach. So from that principles, just do whatever is required to complete job or your work. Never overwork. It's already predestined. Am I correct in the approach Prabhu? This is referring to the five factors of action, five factors of success in an action that Krishna talks about: Adhisthana, Kartha, Karana, Cheshta, and Daiva. Yes, it is in fact an intelligent question that what we are destined to get will actually come. But there is also a certain duty that we all have to perform. We must do our work dutifully. And as long as we have done the duty to the best of our ability, because Cheshta is also one of the factors. And in the scheme of things, we have, it is our role that we have to bring our Cheshta. That's the way the world is organized. Unless that Cheshta is there, that one of the four or five components is there, you will not have result. And hence we have to do, it is ordained on us. It is our responsibility to bring that Cheshta in the form of our endeavor, in the form of our duty. And there is no need to over endeavor, because over endeavor is not going to enhance your result. So we must do our duty. We must do as much work as it is needed of us. And the very famous quote that Srila Prabhupada gave was stuktasya simhasya pravishanti na pravishanti mukhem rukhaha. Simha is considered to be the king in the jungle. He is the lion. But even the lion has to go hunting. Even though the king of the jungle has to go hunting. If the king of the jungle thinks that I am the king after all, I will just lie down here with my mouth open and some animal will enter in my mouth and I will eat him. No. Nahi stuktasya simhasya pravishanti na pravishanti mukhem rukhaha. A rukha will not come and pravishanti because you are the king, you are the king of the jungle, I will come and you please eat me. It is not going to happen. So that is the way the material universe is designed. We have to do our cheshta, our effort is also an important factor. And there is no need to over endeavor because what we are due to get is already destined.

Are the four factors also dependent on daiva? You see daiva, Prabhupada also explains in the purport in the Bhagavad Gita, daiva is considered to be the super cause. If the four factors of action are there and if the fifth factor is not there, then it will not result in the success. But suppose daiva is there and these four factors will somehow come about and even if there is some lacking in it, daiva factors is so powerful, it's because it's called the super cause, it will result in the success of that work. I've come across some people, I remember long, long ago, there was a life member, a very rich man. And then I would go and meet him and many devotees used to meet him also. So, you can see here, his daiva factor is so powerful and he has to get that result. So he may not be very intelligent, he may not be hardworking, but things will fall in his place. So that's why daiva is considered to be a super cause of the four things, of the five things.

### karma, daiva, devotees
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/9p0dGnuA05M?t=2224
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Daiva factor is nothing but the law of karma, deciding what different living entities should get in this material world."
**Summary:** The speaker explains that Daiva is generally a manifestation of the law of karma, except for devotees, where Krishna may intervene based on their devotion and service.

So, how does daiva manifest, and how is it related to karma? Actually, daiva is a manifestation of law of karma, except for devotees. For devotees, they get a certain result, not strictly according to the law of karma, because Krishna becomes involved in it. But otherwise, by and large, daiva factor is nothing but the law of karma, deciding what different living entities should get in this material world. So, you can replace daiva with karma, law of karma. That is karmana daivane trena, that the law of karma is being supervised and implemented by the Lord as Paramatma, seated in the heart of every living entity. So, he is playing that role, except in the case of devotees. For devotees, Krishna sees the laws of karma, and then he also sees the devotees' determination, wanting to serve, his surrender to serve the Lord and the Lord's representative. Then Krishna will interfere, even though that karma won't permit him to experience certain kind of a situation, Krishna will allow that to happen, because he is serving the Lord's mission. This can happen only for bhaktas, for devotees, who are trying to please Krishna, who are serving Krishna's mission. For them, Krishna manifests this exemption clause. Otherwise, everybody is strictly under the laws of karma, from an ant to a devata, to a big demigod.
