### purpose of life, materialism, detachment
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/9p0dGnuA05M?t=2656
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Even if you say they have gone to the moon, they went there and came back, what did they bring?"
**Summary:** The speaker addresses the question of whether man went to the moon, arguing that even if true, the endeavor distracts from the ultimate purpose of life: understanding God and reviving our relationship with Him.

This is a very famous question. Did man go to the moon? And Prabhupada said, how can they go to the moon? And so on. How do we understand this? Yeah, this is a very, very common question that devotees come across. Prabhupada was there in 1966, 65, 66, when this moon landing project was happening by NASA in America. And so there are many arguments that Prabhupada gave. But then one very important argument that Prabhupada gave, which is actually very important. And he said, even if you have gone to the moon, Prabhupada's question was, what is ultimately the benefit of such an elaborate exercise? Because you go there for a short while and you come back. You can't stay there. You can't, you know, the environment is not conducive for us to live there. So, Prabhupada is coming from the point of view that human life is very valuable. We only have some number of years. And we get an opportunity to understand the purpose of life, with the help of the Vedic literatures. Instead of being absorbed in this activity, if we start creating some fancy projects that I have to go to the moon, I have to go to the Mars, I have to go to the Venus, I have to go here, I have to go there, and all of those kind of things. Maybe from a scientific and a technological point of view, it's very challenging and brings lot of people together. You see, why governments encourage these kind of things? Because it brings a lot of people together. You know, just like cricket match. If India wins against Pakistan, then all Indians come together. We feel, oh, we did this. And, you know, it feels, it brings all of us together. There is some kind of a solidarity as countrymen, as Indians. It has those kind of advantages. It helps to manage the world. Otherwise, too many things, you know, India, Pakistan, and all those kind of things. Other kinds of problems can come about. So, it may bring us, it may give that kind of a sense. We as Indians, we did this. We as Americans, we did this. That's how, all these kind of, you know, good feelings, one may, it may generate. But, from a transcendental point of view, from an ultimate point of view, you know, one day, we all have to leave this body and go on to another situation. If we didn't understand the purpose of life, what was God's creed, the purpose when he created this universe, created all of us, if we have missed that arm, we have missed something so important. And we got distracted into all of these other kinds of activities. That is what is so important. That's the point Prabhupada brings up. Even if you say they have gone to the moon, they went there and came back, what did they bring? They brought some rocks. And then, what is that? Is this the most important thing? This is the most important thing in life. There are much more important things in life to understand who I am, to understand the world, the purpose of the world, and to revive our relationship with the Supreme Lord who is waiting for us. And after doing all of this, we take another body and again suffer in another kind of existence. So, the purpose of life is lost in this kind of exciting engagement. It could be, it could be in the form of a moon mission or it could be some cricket mission, it could be some other industry mission or this or that. Human mind is like that. apasyatam atvatatvam. When the human's mind is not aware, enlightened about the truth of the soul, he creates innumerable activities in this world and becomes himself very busy with those kind of things. So, this is one more such activity that a foolish living entity, conditioned soul, not understanding the whole purpose of life develops as some kind of a grandoise activity and governments support that and institutions, mainstream institutions in the world, all of that support that. So, it may have its place, but from a transcendental point of view, we see that we have missed out something very important.

## Qualifications to understand Bhagavad-gita | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### devotion, friendship, non-envy, confidential knowledge
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/MGm-ualXHyE?t=0
**Verse References:** BG 4.3, BG 9.1
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Being a devotee in a transcendental relationship and not being envious of Krishna, these are the qualifications one must have in order to access the confidential knowledge of the Bhagavad Gita."
**Summary:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa explains that devotion and a friendly relationship with Krishna, along with a lack of envy, are essential qualifications for understanding the confidential knowledge of the Bhagavad Gita, based on Krishna's statements in the fourth and ninth chapters.

In the fourth chapter, Krishna says, 'Bhaktosime Sakacheti Rahasyam Hetaduttamam.' Arjuna, this is a confidential knowledge, but you can understand because you are my devotee and friend. So, devotion to Krishna in a transcendental relationship, like a friendship relationship, is an important qualification to access that confidential knowledge. Later on, in the ninth chapter, Krishna says, 'Idam Tute Guhyatamam Pravakshyamyana Suyave.' There also he says, this is very confidential knowledge, but Arjuna, you can understand because you are not envious of me. So, being a devotee in a transcendental relationship and not being envious of Krishna, these are the qualifications one must have in order to access the confidential knowledge of the Bhagavad Gita.

So Prabhupada had come at that age to a foreign land like America, to share this knowledge about Krishna and as taught by Chaitanya Mahaprabhu. And so at some point he introduced the form of worship that Chaitanya had introduced, a very celebratory form of worship, singing and even dancing. And those young American followers, not all of them were very committed, but some of them were very devoted and they had started singing and dancing. And Srila Prabhupada had introduced a certain routine those days. On Mondays, Wednesdays and Fridays he would have a gathering in the evening at 7 o'clock. Some of his very close, who were more devoted and dedicated, they would come by 6 o'clock and there was a two bedroom apartment behind that temple, just behind where Prabhupada was living. And they would all assemble there at 6 o'clock and Prabhupada would do an offering. He would do an aarati, he would offer an incense for a picture of Krishna. So they were all watching and understanding and how Swamiji is doing all of that. And then at 7 o'clock Prabhupada would come down from his apartment to this storefront. And by then, maybe 20, 30, 50 young Americans, boys and girls, they would have assembled. And Srila Prabhupada would sing bhajan. And some of his older followers would sing bhajan. And some of his younger devotees, they would stand up and do this kirtan, swami step, simple dancing, and all of that. And some of his older followers, they would stand up and do this kirtan, swami step, simple dancing, and all of that.

### ISKCON history, Srila Prabhupada, kirtan, New York Times
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/oDYAcTERT3k?t=1274
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers, General public
**Key Quote:** "It brings a state of ecstasy said Allen Ginsberg the poet who was one of the celebrants."

### deity installation, devotee service, traveling
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/eD7m1qxBJ-w?t=117
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "It was quite a tiring experience for Madhudvisha Swami."
**Summary:** Madhudvisha Swami accompanies Srila Prabhupada to Nairobi to install deities, enduring a tiring journey carrying the deities onto the aircraft.

It was going to be a two weeks visit from Bombay to Nairobi and back. Generally, when Srila Prabhupada traveled, there would be his secretary traveling with him, there would be his assistant who would take care of cooking and such things, and there would be a third person, a Sanskrit scholar like Pradyumna, who would help him to go on with the translation of Srimad Bhagavatam. Since Srila Prabhupada was just going to Nairobi and come back to Bombay, it was decided that just one devotee would travel with him, and that one devotee who would travel with him was supposed to be an able body, strong body, is known as the American disciple, Madhudvishaswami. There was a reason why he was chosen to be with Prabhupada. Prabhupada was going to Nairobi to install deities of Radha and Krishna, but somehow, when those deities were bought from Jaipur and shipped to Nairobi, when they opened the cargo, they found that unfortunately the soft marble deities had cracked. So they had to get another set of deities and Madudvisha Swami was in Jaipur, and so he quickly ran around, met a few, visited a few places where these marble deities are made, and got hold of about three and a half feet high Radha Krishna deities, and they were packed. Shrila Prabhupada, these deities were supposed to go to Nairobi. So it was just two of them, Shrila Prabhupada and Madhudvisha Swami, traveling to Nairobi, and they had decided to carry the deities with them in the cabin, not any packaged or any such thing, checked in baggage or anything. So Shrila Prabhupada was heading towards the aircraft and Madhudvisha Swami, he carried the deity one at a time, and he had to go all the way, all the immigration, customs, and clearance and all of that, and then he had to lift it up, carry it up the stairs to the aircraft, and Prabhupada sat there and in front of him he placed one of the deities and then he came back all the way, and he had to pick up another deities and go through the same thing and carry all by himself, and he took the second deity, sat next to Prabhupada, put the deity. It was quite a tiring experience for Madhudvisha Swami, and then the aircraft took off, and they were about, they were going to fly over the Indian Ocean, and then Shrila Prabhupada looked at Meduvre Vishaswamy.

## Srila Prabhupada Stories 3: 120 Chapatis and more

### Srila Prabhupada's compassion, Krishna Prasadam, compromise
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/zAtcWy1Fz7g?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "I have come to, I represent this great tradition from India and I want to present it as it is."
**Summary:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa describes Srila Prabhupada's early days in the West, his strict adherence to principles, and his use of Krishna Prasadam to attract followers.

Hare Krishna. Very nice to be with all of you. We will talk a little bit about Srila Prabhupada's pastimes. When Srila Prabhupada went to the Western countries for the first time in 1965 and in the early years, 65, 66 at that time, Srila Prabhupada represented an ancient, pure, Vedic tradition of Chaitanya Sampradaya and he wanted to share that knowledge. For the young Americans who were coming to him, he was gradually telling them about philosophy and some of the principles, and one of them was to give up meat eating. In the Western countries, there is so much rampant meat eating and it was a big thing for people to give up. In fact, Prabhupada had these four principles: no intoxication, no alcohol, no coffee, tea, no cigarettes, and no meat eating; no gambling; and no illicit connection with women. Many times, some of the elderly people would say, well, I don't want to eat meat. There were many people who came and met Srila Prabhupada. There was one lawyer who was trying to help Srila Prabhupada establish, incorporate the society and he said, if you have these rules, you won't be able to attract Americans. Maybe you should not have these rules at all. Prabhupada was not ready to compromise. He said that, I represent this great tradition from India and I want to present it as it is. If Americans are not happy with it, I'll go back to my country. Just for the sake of Americans, just to attract them, I cannot make compromises and dilute the principles. So Srila Prabhupada was very strict about these things. But one great arsenal Srila Prabhupada had with him, and that was Krishna Prasadam. Prabhupada would cook himself in the very early days. There was no one else. He would cook himself. And then these few of the young followers, American men and young boys and girls, and he would serve them Prasadam. Some of them were gradually taking it seriously. They had given up meat and they were liking the Prasadam that Prabhupada was making. You must know Srila Prabhupada was an excellent cook. You can imagine that an excellent cook like Srila Prabhupada, and he prepares, and then he offers it to Krishna, his dear Lord, what should be the effect, what should be the Prasadam quality there. It was simply unbelievable. It was completely out of the world. These young Americans, they were actually sold out on that. They would eat a lot because American food, Western food is quite bland, unlike Indian food, which is very spicy. Some of them began to like the spicy food and they would eat well. One of the devotees recalls that those days there were about 10, 12 of them who ate Prasadam. There were 10, 12 of them who would come regularly, every day. There would be more when there were big gatherings. These 10, 12 of them would come up to Srila Prabhupada's apartment and Prabhupada would cook lunch for them. These young American boys and girls, they were very hungry and they had switched over from all the meat eating and all of that to vegetarian diet. Srila Prabhupada would make rotis and chapatis. They were very hungry. Each one would eat about 10 to 12 chapatis. They were serving hungry. Srila Prabhupada was making all of that. The devotees later on, they recall that Prabhupada was making something like 120 chapatis all alone. He would make the dal, he would make the rice, he would make the sabji and all of that and make it available for these young American followers, his students and they would relish that. You can see the kind of effort and the sacrifice that Srila Prabhupada was making. He's a learned scholar. He's an author of books. He is 71 years old at that time. He's gone from India to America, from Vrindavan. In fact, those days, I met those young Americans. They would ask him, what is Vrindavan like? Prabhupada would say, I will take you one day and show you Vrindavan. How wonderful Vrindavan is. You will wonder, how did Swamiji leave Vrindavan and come to this terrible place called New York City? That's Vrindavan. This is the way Srila Prabhupada explained. The kind of compassion and sacrifice. What is the kind of sacrifice Prabhupada was making to spread Krishna Bhakti in a foreign land? Prabhupada made this very delicious Krishna Prasadam and they would be attracted to Krishna Prasadam. They would be attracted to Kirtan. They would be attracted to the philosophy Srila Prabhupada was teaching. Above all of this, they were drawn and attracted to Srila Prabhupada as a person, very compassionate, very learned, taking all the trouble and giving all the time to explain all the nuances of the philosophy and the doubts that they would have and so they were really drawn to Srila Prabhupada.

---

You may remember that how Srila Prabhupada when initially when devotees went to Africa they had very good reception from Gujaratis and a few other Indian gentlemen and well-established in Africa, several generations, lot of a lot of Indians are there in Nairobi, Mombasa, Kenya and a few other countries in Africa, South Africa. Prabhupada said it was you know Africans cooking some Indian food and they are not trained in it and Prabhupada called it pig food, suitable for horses, dog food and then when all that and then we know how Srila Prabhupada himself went into the kitchen and all these 12 Africans were there and he was teaching them how to do cooking. Can you imagine this? You can see that this is a temple, African Nairobi, a temple there, a temple kitchen, a vegetarian kitchen where Prabhupada is there, sanyasi and he must be around 76 years or so, author of books, rivier sanyasi from India, scholarly and he is surrounded by 12 black Africans and he is teaching them how to do cooking. ### sacrifice, compassion, humility
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/zAtcWy1Fz7g?t=630
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "If there is no well water, we cannot come there, we cannot come out, do our cooking, we cannot come out."
**Summary:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa contrasts Srila Prabhupada's willingness to travel anywhere and adapt to any situation to preach Krishna consciousness with the strict requirements of a Madhva sanyasi.

I'll tell you one interesting interaction that I was a witness to maybe about 20 years ago. There was one quite a senior devotee of ISKCON and I was accompanying him to Udupi ancient Krishna temple of Madh aula одipi ancient Krishna temple of Madh bha chariya Sampradayani and then we were interacting with one sanyasi, Madhva sanyasi, and this senior devotee who was with me from ISKCON and he was talking to him and I was trying to translate that to the language that the sanyasi can understand and so this devotee said Swamiji you must come to America to read this scriptures, let's cutخ Slavim ye the target of your avatars and to the detail of what have you dust and to understand and so this devotee said Swamiji you must come to America, please girl, you must come to America, too and then came along. Swamiji, you must come to America, there is immense preaching field, lot of people want to hear about Krishna and you must come and you are all very learned sanyasis of the Madhva Sampradaya, you are all Vaishnavas. You must come and teach about Krishna to Americans and rest of the world. And so that sanyasi, Madhva sanyasi, very elderly sanyasi, very respectable sanyasi, he said, you see if we have to come, every day, every place, we will need well water. If there is no well water, we cannot come there, we cannot come out, do our cooking, we cannot come out. We cannot do our puja, we cannot come to such place. So I was reflecting, you just see the contrast. Srila Prabhupada has gone to places like New York, Africa and innumerable other western cities and Prabhupada, surrounded by these westerners, he has convinced them to become vegetarians. He is teaching them how to cook Indian food, how to offer to Krishna. How to make it Krishna Prasadam, change their lifestyle. Look at the compassion, look at the sacrifice that Srila Prabhupada is making to spread Krishna consciousness all over the world. Compared to, you know, of course they are all very respectable sadhus are there in our country, very respectable sanyasis, sadhus and different mats and different organizations are there. But just see the... In this, at such an advanced stage, the kind of sacrifice that Srila Prabhupada is making, this is something, you know, extraordinary that Srila Prabhupada did.

### austerity, Krishna Prasadam, consciousness
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/zAtcWy1Fz7g?t=790
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Srila Prabhupada has offered us a spiritual mind where we can, we also make very nice elaborate feast, offer to the Lord."
**Summary:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa shares a conversation among devotees comparing Srila Prabhupada's offering of Krishna Prasadam with the austere practices of another spiritual organization.

I must share another very interesting conversation that happened among the devotees in our temple here in Bangalore, just a few months ago. Bangalore temple devotees, we were all talking. It was in some meeting. And then we strayed off into talking a few other topics other than the main topics in the meeting, formal temple meeting. The discussion came up about one other spiritual organization from our country, very well known. They also have temples around the world and a lot of followers. They also have a lot of their sadhus, they call them followers, their sadhus. The discussion came up that how these sadhus of this organization, I don't want to mention the organization, very respectable, nice people, well known to us also. These sadhus of that organization, they are very austere. We learned that what they do, they have a feast and they offer that on special days, you know, like Ram Navami or something. They have their offering and they make a feast. Finally, the sadhus in the ashram. The sadhus in the ashram, what they do is that there's a big feast. Now they mix all the feasts, daal, sabji, gulab jamun, khichdi, shaag, bonda, pakoda, whatever. Everything, they mix it up, mash it up like that. Then pour water and then drink it. So that, you know, they don't enjoy the feast. They enjoy their senses eating good food or something like that. Very impressive, isn't it? Very austere. When we were talking about this, one of the devotees in our meeting group said, Wow, these sadhus, they are so austere. Oh my God, they just can't even have a feast. They do this every day. They have a bowl, supposedly. Whatever it fills in that bowl, only that much they can eat. They can't even take more than that. You can't overeat. You have to, this kind of a mashed food you have to eat every day. Oh my God, what an austerity. One of the devotees who heard this very spontaneously said, My God, next time I see these sadhus, I'll offer my pranams to them and tell them, Wow, hats off to the austerity that you are practicing. Another devotee commented, Look at what Srila Prabhupada said. Srila Prabhupada is offering us. Srila Prabhupada has offered us a spiritual mind where we can, we also make very nice elaborate feast, offer to the Lord. We also relish Krishna Prasadam with all of the very gatedness. After having enjoyed this wonderful Krishna Prasadam, Srila Prabhupada is offering us a state of consciousness far, far higher than all of these other sadhus and spiritual organizations are offering. So, Unnata Ujjvala Rasa Swabhakti Shriyam. This is what the Acharyas have explained.

### Krishna Bhakti, Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, Vedic treasure
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/zAtcWy1Fz7g?t=1036
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers, General public
**Key Quote:** "It is the duty of Indians to share this wealth, this treasure from the Vedic literatures."
**Summary:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa emphasizes that Krishna consciousness is the highest state of consciousness, a treasure from the Vedic literatures brought out by Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, and that it is the duty of Indians to share this with the world.

Everyone said, yes, we should offer our lives to Srila Prabhupada. Even that's not enough to repay what Srila Prabhupada has given us. Krishna consciousness that Srila Prabhupada was giving, was teaching around the world was something, it's a most elevated state of consciousness that the Vedic literatures talk about. Unnata Ujjvala Rasa Swabhakti Shriyam. That is the treasure. This is a treasure in the Vedic literatures. That treasure in the Vedic literatures was not known to many people. Chaitanya Mahaprabhu brought out that treasure. He wanted people to experience that. It was Chaitanya Mahaprabhu's desire that this treasure from the Vedic literatures is shared with the whole world. Everywhere in the world there are seekers. There are people who are looking for spiritual truths, spiritual knowledge, spiritual understanding. It is the duty of Indians to share this wealth, this treasure from the Vedic literatures.

### transcendental meditation, Krishna consciousness, preaching
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/zAtcWy1Fz7g?t=1107
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Newcomers, General public
**Key Quote:** "So many of Srila Prabhupada's young American followers, they were all, formerly they had had some kind of an exposure to Transcendental Meditation."
**Summary:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa explains how Srila Prabhupada encountered Transcendental Meditation and Maharishi Mahesh Yogi in the West and how it was a common topic of discussion with his early followers.

When Srila Prabhupada went to America in 1965-66, one of the things that a common theme that Srila Prabhupada would come across was, there was one other spiritual organization from India, Maharshi Mahesh Yogi. He had popularized what was known as TM, Transcendental Meditation. So many of Srila Prabhupada's young American followers, they were all, formerly they had had some kind of an exposure to Transcendental Meditation. Invariably in the question-answer session with Srila Prabhupada, they would bring up these questions about TM, Transcendental Meditation, and what is meditation. All of these kind of topics would very often come. Srila Prabhupada was hearing about Transcendental Meditation and Maharshi, and he also had established many centers in Western countries, in America, in Europe, and other places. Prabhupada had heard about that quite often. A few other organizations like that, but definitely Maharshi, Mahesh Yogi's Transcendental Meditation was quite well known among the young Americans. Much later, Srila Prabhupada was in Atlanta temple. This was March of 1975. So you can imagine, 1966 the temple was, ISKCON was incorporated. Now we are talking about 1975. Nine years have passed. ISKCON has spread around the world. Prabhupada has so many followers around the world. Prabhupada had come to Atlanta temple. Devotees brought one young American, who had become a devotee. They introduced him to Srila Prabhupada. They said, Prabhupada, Srila Prabhupada, this is Doug. An American name, common name, Doug. This is Doug. He has become a devotee of Krishna now. He is in the temple now. He was closely associated with the Mahesh Yogi's philosophy. He was, for two years, his personal secretary. Traveling with him, being with him, helping him in all his different activities and projects and all of that. Maharshi had created an executive council to help him reach out to the universities and create courses and all of those kind of things. That council was called the 108. It's not that it had 108 people, but it was called the 108. All of these kind of topics would very often come. Srila Prabhupada was hearing about transcendental meditation and Maharshi. He also had established many centers in Western countries, in America, in Europe and other places. Prabhupada had heard about that quite often. A few other organizations like that. But definitely Maharshi, Mahesh Yogi's transcendental meditation was quite well known among the young Americans.

That was the residence of Advaita Acharya in Shantipur. Even now there is a temple of Chaitanya Mahaprabhu and Advaita Acharya. He wouldn't talk much to anybody. He would come on the weekends and he would be there for a few hours and then he would be seen sitting and very intently chanting, chanting. As a Poojari he would move around and then he would see and then he also saw that there were times when he was he saw this Bengali gentleman in khadi dress white dress and he would be chanting and there were tears in his eyes as he is chanting and he wouldn't disturb him because he was silently sitting and chanting. Just before he left after his chanting he would come and meet the meet him and with folded hands and then and appreciate him that he was doing puja here in this temple very important temple. I also wouldn't talk too much because he looked like he wanted to be to himself and then he would go away. Every now and then forties fifties he would see this elderly this middle aged person come and chant for a few hours and with tears in his eyes very feelingly chant and go away. Then for some time he stopped seeing him he was not coming at all and then he remembers it was August of 1965 so this sevait pujari he was doing his puja he was attending to the temple and suddenly he saw at the far end of the temple once again that same person has come but now he is in saffron robes and so he saw him and then he was sitting not in white khadi kurta and khadi dhoti but now he is in saffron dress and he was chanting chanting chanting and on that particular day he chanted for a long time and then so he didn't disturb him and then he came after the chanting he came and he paid obeisance to the deities there and he paid obeisance unusually long obeisance and then as a pujari he was watching all that and then he talked to him and then he spoke to him and he said yes I see you are the same person who used to come before and then he asked him what is your name who are you and then that saffron clad sadhu sanyasi he said my name is my name is Bhaktivedanta Swami and I have been ordered by my revered spiritual master Bhaktivedanta Saraswati Goswami Maharaj and he has given me an impossible mission to accomplish he has asked me to spread Krishna consciousness all over the discussions would happen they would be planning how we can inundate the world with love of Krishna and so this place is very special so I come here and chant praying for their mercy praying for their direction how I can ever accomplish this impossible mission my Guru Maharaj has asked me to do to spread Krishna consciousness all over the world and he said tomorrow from Calcutta I am boarding a a ### Vaishnava tradition, servant of God, philosophy
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/vIdSB_kWFg4?t=1312
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "If someone says he is God, he is not God."
**Summary:** The speaker explains Srila Prabhupada's strong refutation of the idea that one can become God through meditation, emphasizing the Vaishnava understanding of being a servant of God.

and should be asked. Srila Prabhupada would strongly speak about this. This is a philosophy that's not explained in the Gita and not explained in the Vaishnava tradition. According to the Vaishnava tradition, according to the Bhagavad Gita, we are all part and parcel of Krishna. We are servant of Krishna. Krishna is the Supreme Master. Prabhupada often quoted verses from the Upanishads, Nithyo Nithyanam, Chetanas Chetananam, Eko Bahunam, Yo Vidha Dati Kamar, Katha Upanishad, where it says that the living entities are many and there is the Lord who is one, both of them are eternal and they are eternally the same. The Lord will eternally be the Lord and the living entity part and parcel will eternally be the part and parcel. The Lord is conscious, the living entity is conscious, Chetanas Chetananam, Nithyo Nithyanam, Chetanas Chetananam, eternal and eternal, Eko Bahunam, Yo Vidha Dati Kamar and that one is the provider of everything that the many conscious eternal entities want or desire. So one is the supplier, one is the receiver. The supplier, the receiver cannot become the supplier, he is always eternally the receiver. So these kind of ideas Srila Prabhupada had often talked about and then Prabhupada would often say. If somebody says, I am God, you know, it's an absurd statement. I realize God, I meditate on God and I become God. You know what God is? God controls the planetary movements. And I start controlling the planetary movements. What kind of an absurdity that is? Is the sun going to listen to me? Unless I am some insane guy thinking that I have become God, now I have God realized and I'm controlling all the stars and the planets and the moon and all of those kind of things. How absurd it is. So Prabhupada would strongly speak against this kind of an understanding and say, no, from the Bhagavad Gita, from the teachings of the Vedic literatures, we understand we are not God. We are servant of God. We are of the quality of God, but not God. God is God. We are always his part, amsa, mamai vamsho jiva loke, jivabhuta sanatana. This is Krishna's instruction in the Gita. Sanatana we are amsa, eternally we are amsa. And his amsa, he is the purna, he is the full. So this is the philosophy Prabhupada often would talk. And then sometimes, very often these questions would come about. Someone would come and declare that I have been practicing yoga for the last one year. And I have become God. You know, all those kind of things that these kind of people would come and declare. So Prabhupada would strongly say, if someone says he is God, he is not God. He is the opposite. Not G-O-D. He is D-O-G. You know, these kind of very, very strong themes that Prabhupada would talk about. In all of his classes. And so these young Americans, they would hear about all these things and then oh, Swamiji says that we are not God. We are actually servant of God and all of those kind of things. So it was one of the popular themes that Srila Prabhupada had repeatedly stressed in his classes, in his discussions and question answers and all of that.

### women, Gayatri Mantra, time place circumstance

One should install the physical form of the Lord and with the chanting of the Mantra, one should offer flowers and fruits and other varieties of foodstuffs exactly according to the rules and regulations prescribed by the authorities. But this should be done in consideration of place, time and attendant conveniences and inconveniences. And Prabhupada explains here now according to because it says Desha Kala Vibhagavit and Saparyam Vividhair Dravyaer Desha Kala Vibhagavit. The paraphernalia Dravya that you use should be according to Desha Kala, according to practical circumstances and all of those kind of things. ### transcendence, anger, absolute truth
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/DgwYgDv6gTw?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Because he is absolute, both his anger and pleasure are the same."
**Summary:** This segment explains that while both Arjuna and Krishna appear angry, Krishna's anger is transcendental and not subject to material nature.

Both Arjuna and Lord Shri Krishna are described here in an angry mood. But Arjuna's eyes were like balls of red copper, whereas the eyes of the Lord were like lotuses. This means that the angry mood of Arjuna and that of the Lord are not on the same level. The Lord is Transcendence. Please note, Transcendence with a capital T. The Lord is Transcendence. I hope it's the same there, yeah. And thus he is absolute in any stage. His anger is not like the anger of a conditioned living being within the modes of qualitative material nature. Because he is absolute, both his anger and pleasure are the same. His anger is not exhibited in the three modes of material nature. It is only a sign of his bent of mind towards the cause of his devotee because that is his transcendental nature. Therefore, even if he is angry, the object of anger is blessed. He is unchanged in all circumstances.

When the Kumaras, although by far the fittest persons, were thus forbidden entrance by the two of them, the two chief doorkeepers of Sri Hari, while other divinities looked on, their eyes suddenly turned red because of anger, due to their great eagerness to see their most beloved master, Sri Hari, the personality of Godhead.

---
### renunciation, anger, Krishna consciousness
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/HdPMySPtJv4?t=103
**Verse References:** BG 9.29
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The difference between the anger of an ordinary person and that of a liberated person is that an ordinary person becomes angry because his sense desires are not being fulfilled, whereas a liberated person like the Kumaras becomes angry when restricted in the discharge of duties for serving the Supreme Personality of Godhead."
**Summary:** The speaker reads Srila Prabhupada's purport, explaining the role of a sanyasi in Vedic society, the importance of Krishna as the best friend, and the nature of anger in both conditioned and liberated souls, emphasizing that even liberated persons can experience anger when service to the Lord is obstructed.

Purport by Srila Prabhupada. According to the Vedic system, a sanyasi, a person in the renounced order of life, is dressed in saffron-colored garments. This saffron dress is practically a passport for the mendicant and sanyasi to go anywhere. The sanyasi's duty is to enlighten people in Krishna consciousness. Those in the renounced order of life have no other business but preaching the glories and supremacy of the Supreme Personality of Godhead. Therefore, the Vedic sociological conception is that a sanyasi should not be restricted. He is allowed to go anywhere and everywhere he wants, and he is not refused any gift he might demand from a householder. The four Kumaras came to see the Supreme Personality of Godhead, Narayana. The word Suhrtama, best of all friends, is important. As Lord Krishna states in the Bhagavad Gita, He is the best friend of all living entities. suhrtam sarva-bhuta-anam. No one can be a greater well-wishing friend to any living entity than the Supreme Personality of Godhead. He is so kindly disposed towards everyone that in spite of our completely forgetting our relationship with the Supreme Lord, He comes Himself. Sometimes personally, as Lord Krishna appeared on this earth, and sometimes as His devotee, as did Lord Chaitanya Mahaprabhu, and sometimes He sends His bona fide devotees to reclaim all the fallen souls. Therefore, He is the greatest well-wishing friend of everyone. And the Kumaras wanted to see Him. The doorkeepers should have known that the four sages had no other business, and therefore to restrict them from entering the palace was not apt. In this verse, it is figuratively stated that the younger brother of desire suddenly appeared in person when the sages were forbidden to see their most beloved personality of Godhead. The younger brother of desire is anger. If one's desire is not fulfilled, the younger brother anger follows. Here we can mark that even great saintly persons like the Kumaras were also angry, but they were not angry for their personal interests. They were angry because they were forbidden to enter the palace to see the personality of Godhead. Therefore, the theory that in the perfectional stage one should not have anger is not supported in this verse. Anger will continue even in the liberated stage.

---
### liberation, sense control, Krishna consciousness
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/HdPMySPtJv4?t=294
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Becoming liberated does not necessitate losing one's sensual activities. Sense activities continue even in the liberated stage. The difference is however that sense activities in liberation are accepted only in connection with Krishna Consciousness, whereas sense activities in the conditioned stage are enacted for personal sense gratification."
**Summary:** The speaker continues reading Srila Prabhupada's purport, clarifying that liberated persons like the Kumaras can still experience anger, but their anger is directed towards serving the Lord, not personal gratification. He emphasizes that liberation doesn't eliminate sensual activities but transforms them into Krishna consciousness.

These four mendicant brothers, the Kumaras, were considered liberated persons, but still they were angry because they were restricted in their service to the Lord. The difference between the anger of an ordinary person and that of a liberated person is that an ordinary person becomes angry because his sense desires are not being fulfilled, whereas a liberated person like the Kumaras becomes angry when restricted in the discharge of duties for serving the Supreme Personality of Godhead. In the previous verse, it has been clearly mentioned that the Kumaras were liberated persons. Vidit Atma Tatva means one who understands the truth of self-realization. One who does not understand the truth of self-realization is called ignorant. But one who understands the self, the super-self, their inter-relation and activities in self-realization is called Vidit Atma Tatva. Although the Kumaras were already liberated persons, they nevertheless became angry. This point is very important. Becoming liberated does not necessitate losing one's sensual activities. Sense activities continue even in the liberated stage. The difference is however that sense activities in liberation are accepted only in connection with Krishna Consciousness, whereas sense activities in the conditioned stage are enacted for personal sense gratification.

**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Why is it that the sages should be allowed to go anywhere and no one should stop them? Because the sages are carriers of the message of the Lord. They have no interest other than to share the information about the Supreme Lord, the purpose of life and what is that we should do in this human form of life."
**Summary:** The speaker transitions to discussing Prabhupada's points, emphasizing that sages should not be forbidden from entering places because they carry the message of the Lord and enlighten society. He explains the Vedic sociological conception and the important position of sadhus in sharing spiritual knowledge.

So Prabhupada has touched upon many important points. The first one is that the sages were not to be forbidden because it is so in the, it is the sanyasi or a mendicant or a sage is permitted to go to any place and no one shall stop them. That is the, what Prabhupada has said here. This is the Vedic sociological conception. How a Vedic society is organized, how the Vedic society conducts is what is being described. Why is it so? Why is it that the sages should be allowed to go anywhere and no one should stop them? Because the sages are carriers of the message of the Lord. They have no interest other than to share the information about the Supreme Lord, the purpose of life and what is that we should do in this human form of life. So they have, they are meant to enlighten the society and hence they should not be stopped. This is the important position of the sadhus in the Vedic sociological conception.

### Vedic society, brahmanas, self-realization
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/HdPMySPtJv4?t=786
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** story
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Giving knowledge about self-realization is even far superior and more important than becoming a king and ruling over a kingdom."
**Summary:** The speaker illustrates the importance of saintly persons in Vedic society by narrating the story of King Vena, who was killed by brahmanas for being impious. He explains that the brahmanas did not become king themselves because they had more important duties related to self-realization and teaching others.

From this we see, the important position given to a saintly person in the Vedic society. He is discharging a very important duty of enlightening the people about the spiritual values of life. In another place, in the Bhagavatam, King Vena was a very impious king. And then, in the Vedic system, the king has to follow the directions of the brahmanas and rule and encourage and not only maintain the citizens in his kingdom, fulfilling their material needs, he also has an obligation to ensure that their spiritual needs are also fulfilled. But King Vena was not a good king. He was a sinful person and he didn't care for the brahmanas and he was not encouraging any spiritual activities in his kingdom. At that time, all the brahmanas in his kingdom come together and they discuss what is to be done. And they decide that they should kill King Vena. And they kill him. And then, it says, from Vena's body they created another person and made him the king. Now the question comes, if the brahmanas were so powerful that they could kill and dethrone a king, why couldn't they become the king themselves? After dethroning King Vena, because after all he was a bad king. And there Prabhupada explains, no, the brahmanas would not become the king because they had more important duties than becoming a king, which is, they were engaged in self-realization and they were engaged in teaching others in the society in the matter of self-realization. So you see from all of these kind of instructions, where Srila Prabhupada positions that activity of giving knowledge about self-realization is. It's even far superior and more important than becoming a king and ruling over a kingdom. So this is the kind of conception that Srila Prabhupada in all his teachings he brings about, about the role of a saintly person in the human society. And hence in the Vedic conception, such a saintly person should have free access to move around in the human society and give this knowledge to whoever was ready to receive this.

And here we see Krishna is the best well-wishing friend of all living entities. And Krishna the Supreme Lord the Supreme Powerful Lord He has sanctioned such a misery to a family. Everyone is suffering. Why is this so? How do we understand why the Lord has sanctioned such intense suffering that people are crying so much? Why there is death like this?

### impurity, desire, sense gratification, Krishna consciousness
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/LfFYYZdRfuk?t=0
**Verse References:** BG 7.27
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Training in Krishna consciousness will help one be promoted to Vaikuntha."
**Summary:** This segment introduces the Srimad Bhagavatam verse and explains how impurity leads to material existence and how Krishna consciousness can lead to Vaikuntha.

Reading from Srimad Bhagavatam, Canto 3, Chapter 15, Text number 34. He is stated in Bhagavad Gita, 7th Chapter, Verse 27. It is stated that as long as a living entity is pure, he is in complete harmony with the desires of the Supreme Lord, but as soon as he becomes impure, he is in disharmony with the desires of the Lord. By contamination, he is forced to transfer to this material world, where the living entities have three enemies, namely, desire, anger, and lust. These three enemies force the living entities to continue material existence, and when one is free from them, he is eligible to enter the kingdom of God. One should not, therefore, be angry in the absence of an opportunity for sense gratification, and one should not be lusty to acquire more than necessary. In this verse, it is clearly stated that the two doormen should be sent into the material world, where criminals are allowed to reside. Since the basic principles of criminality are sense gratification, anger, and unnecessary lust, persons conducted by these three enemies of the living entity are never promoted to Vaikunthaloka. People should learn Bhagavad Gita and accept the Supreme Personality of Godhead Krishna as the Lord of everything. They should practice satisfying the senses of the Supreme Lord instead of trying to satisfy their own senses. Training in Krishna consciousness will help one be promoted to Vaikuntha. Thus ends the Bhaktivedanta purport.

---

If they're in the spiritual world, the moral Ninevayas must be perfect. But, they fall to the material world. How does that happen? So that is explained in the seventh chapter of the Bhagavad Gita. ### desire, envy, supreme, duality
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/LfFYYZdRfuk?t=755
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Itchha means desire...specifically referring to desire to become the supreme."
**Summary:** This segment elaborates on the concepts of itchha (desire) and dvesha (envy), explaining how they contribute to the delusion of duality and the desire to become supreme, which is contrary to the natural inclination of a living entity to serve the Lord.

Just like here, antarabhava drishtya. So as living entities, we are part and parcel of the Lord. It is natural that we must have an interest like the Lord. Our interest must be perfectly aligned with the interest of the Lord. But when we develop a different desire, a different understanding, a different mentality, antarabhava, then that is called dvandva moha. And then, because of that dvandva moha, itchha dvesha samuthena comes about. Prabhupada has explained very nicely what is this itchha dvesha. Itchha means desire. Here it is specifically referring to desire to become the supreme. In fact, if you see in this material world, everyone in every field tries to become the foremost. Businessmen try to become the richest. Students try to become the smartest. Famous people try to become the most famous. Powerful people try to become the most powerful. So they are actually, this is the desire. The living entity is driven by that desire. Itchha. And dvesha is envy of Krishna. When you hear that Krishna is the supreme, the thought, why should I accept Krishna is the supreme? Why Krishna is the supreme? Why can't I be the supreme?

### living entity, Lord, duality, context
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/LfFYYZdRfuk?t=873
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "A living entity is not expected to have this kind of a thinking."
**Summary:** This segment emphasizes that a living entity should naturally serve the Lord, like a part of the body serves the whole, and introduces the importance of understanding the context when reading verses in the Gita, similar to looking at surrounding words in a dictionary.

These two desires, itchha dvesha samuthena dvandva mohena bharata. Actually, a living entity is not expected to have this kind of a thinking. A living entity is part and parcel of the Lord. Just like every part of the body tries to serve the whole body. That is natural. And when the part develops a different attitude, it is called antarabhava drishtya. Dvandva moha. Actually, it's interesting to see in what context Krishna says this. It's good to, like I remember sometime long ago, someone had told, when you read a, when you see a word in a dictionary, like sometime, of course now you don't see a dictionary, all these days are gone. You google. When you see a word in a dictionary, some, you know, some old people's good advice, you see one word before that and one word after that and learn two words, so you learn three words. In the same way, when you read a verse in the Gita, it's good to see one verse before and one verse after. And you'll get to see the context. And it'll help us develop a certain interesting perspective.

Reading from Srimad Bhagavatam, Canto 3, Chapter 15, Text No. 35: teṣām itīritaṁ bhāvava dhārya-gōraṁ tam brahma-dandam anivāraṇaṁ astra-pūgaiḥ sadyo hareranu ca rāvuru bhibhyatāstāt pāda-gṛhāva patatārāṁ tāmatikātare nāṁ teṣām itīritaṁ bhāvava dhārya-gōraṁ tam brahma-dandam anivāraṇaṁ. ### devotion, offenses, consequences
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/U6_43FQ2sh8?t=61
**Verse References:** SB 3.15.35
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "There are many kinds of offences, but the greatest offence is to offend a devotee of the Lord."
**Summary:** The speaker reads Srila Prabhupada's purport, emphasizing the doormen's awareness of their mistake, the gravity of offending a devotee, and their subsequent fear.

When the doormen of Vaikunthaloka, who were certainly devotees of the Lord, found that they were going to be cursed by the brāhmaṇas, they at once became veiled. They were very much afraid and fell down at the feet of the brāhmaṇas in great anxiety. For a brāhmaṇa's curse cannot be counteracted by any kind of weapon. Although by chance the doormen committed a mistake by checking the brāhmaṇas from entering the gate of Vaikuntha, they were at once aware of the gravity of the curse. There are many kinds of offences, but the greatest offence is to offend a devotee of the Lord. Because the doormen were also devotees of the Lord, they were able to understand their mistake and were terrified when the four kumaras were ready to curse them. Thus ends the Bhaktivedanta purport.

### knowledge, truth, guru
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/U6_43FQ2sh8?t=575
**Verse References:** BG 4.34
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "We have to get an understanding of this, of this world, from those who are enlightened."
**Summary:** The speaker uses the analogy of a goldsmith to illustrate the need to seek knowledge from enlightened sources, quoting Krishna's instruction to approach those who have seen the truth (tatvadarshinah).

Just like, if you want to know the value of something, say some ornament, sometimes we, some people drop some jewellery in the hundi, and then when we get that jewellery, and we want to make an estimate, how much it is, is it real gold, or some imitation jewellery, somebody dropped, now if you want to make an estimation of that, you have to go to a goldsmith, a goldsmith will check out, and then, because he is an expert in that, he will tell you, it's worth, how much money. So in the same way, we have to get an estimation of anything, we have to go to a goldsmith. If you go to a blacksmith, and take a piece of jewellery, you are not going to get very good understanding. So in the same way, we have to get an understanding of this, of this world, from those who are enlightened. That is the spirit, that is the perspective, that we must maintain about this material world. Because, if people who don't, who are not enlightened, their views are not very important. That is why, when Krishna says, tad viddhi pranipatena pariprasnena sevaya, upadekshanti te jnanam jnaninas tatvadarshinah. Krishna is using the word, you must approach, tatvadarshinah, those who have, those who have seen the truth. In other words, those who are experiencing the truth, tatvadarshinah, no use going to an ordinary person, if you want to get spiritual knowledge. In this context, Prabhupada also said, we should read books written by tatvadarshis, those who have actually seen the truth, very enlightened people. From their point of view, we should understand our life, our situation, our world, everything. Then, we will be able to derive benefit from that.

### knowledge, desire, action
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/U6_43FQ2sh8?t=730
**Verse References:** BG 4.19
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "One is understood to be in full knowledge, whose every act is devoid of desire for sense gratification."
**Summary:** The speaker references Bhagavad Gita 4.19, explaining that true wisdom is characterized by actions devoid of desire for sense gratification, and that such individuals are recognized as wise by learned men.

There is another verse in the Bhagavad Gita, Krishna refers to the similar thing, that how, actually many times, but in this particular place, yasya sarve samarambha, kama sankalpa varjitaha, jnanagni dhadda karmanam, tamahuhu panditam buddhaha. In the chapter 4, text number 19, this is same as the, tamahuhu panditam buddhaha, these people are considered to be, buddhaha, wise, by panditas. Sometimes somebody may consider them to be a wise man. Right? Like all our parents consider us to be very intelligent, my son is so intelligent. We may not be doing very well, but still our parents, out of love, they may say. So that's not important, we have to, whether we are wise, considered to be buddhaha, by panditas, tamahuhu panditam buddhaha. That is important. So Krishna is saying here, yasya sarve samarambha, kama sankalpa varjitaha, jnanagni dhadda karmanam, tamahuhu panditam buddhaha. In all endeavors, sarve samarambha, in all endeavors, kama sankalpa varjitaha, they have given up the desire for enjoyment, kama, self-enjoyment, or sense gratification. Because in every endeavor, a conditioned soul tries to enjoy. What is it that I can get for my sense gratification? Because that's the nature of the conditioned soul, when we come to spiritual life also, in spiritual life also we will be seeing how I can get some sense gratification. So that's the sad part. That is what we have to be watching out. So, yasya sarve samarambha, kama sankalpa varjitaha.

### knowledge, desire, karma
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/U6_43FQ2sh8?t=871
**Verse References:** BG 4.19
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "If in all our endeavors we are looking for sense gratification, that is an indication we are not situated in jnana, we are still in ajnana."
**Summary:** The speaker continues to elaborate on Bhagavad Gita 4.19, explaining that freedom from desire for sense gratification is a result of being situated in knowledge, and conversely, the pursuit of sense gratification indicates a lack of knowledge.

So they have given up varjitaha, kama sankalpa, that determination or that desire for kama, varjitaha, jnanagni dhadda karmanam, such people who have become free from desire for sense gratification, in all their endeavors, such people have actually burned their fruitive reactions in the fire of knowledge. Which means, Prabhupada points out very nicely, kama sankalpa varjitaha is a result of being situated in jnana. So, if we are situated in transcendental knowledge, the effect of that is, in all our endeavors, we will not be looking for sense gratification. Conversely, if in all our endeavors we are looking for sense gratification, that is an indication we are not situated in jnana, we are still in ajnana. So, this is what great learned men consider. One is understood to be in full knowledge, whose every act is devoid of desire for sense gratification. He is said by sages to be a worker, whose fruitive action is burnt up by the fire of perfect knowledge. So, this kind of a perspective, we must have an understanding, we must have an estimation of this material world. What is this material world about? From the perspective of enlightened people.

### detachment, sense enjoyment, transcendental experience
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/JGJcFBuz4gk?t=1400
**Verse References:** BG 2.59
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "But when you do paramdrishtva when you have the transcendental experience raso api nivartante even the desire even the sense of enjoyment goes away."
**Summary:** The speaker analyzes a verse from the Bhagavad Gita, explaining that while abstaining from sense objects may suppress desires, only transcendental experience can eliminate the taste for sense enjoyment.

It's a very interesting verse the verse talks about two things niraharasya dehinam niraharasya niraharasya one meaning of the word nirahara means not eating food ahara nirahara so not eating food but here niraharasya refers to negative restricting principles negative principles don't do this don't do this vishaya vinivartante niraharasya dehinam rasavarjam rasopyasya here the niraharasya dehinam one who is abstaining following all of these negative restrictions niraharasya dehinam dehinam a person who has an embodied person a living entity niraharasya dehinam vishaya vinivartante rasavarjam vishaya vinivartante vishaya vinivartante means he is abstaining from the vishayas that's what the meaning of niraharasya he is not supplying the vishaya vishaya refers to indriyavishaya so he is abstaining from vishaya vishaya vinivartante niraharasya dehinam rasavarjam only vishaya vinivartante rasavarjam vishaya meaning rasa other than rasa rasavarjam means apart from the sense of enjoyment in other words the sense of enjoyment is still there so he may be niraharasya dehinam vishaya vinivartante but rasavarjam vishaya vinivartante he is still attracted to that rasa for enjoying the vishaya is there other than that other than that he is abstaining from the vishaya but rasopyasya paramdrishtva what is that paramdrishtva nivartante rasopyasya paramdrishtva nivartante but when you do paramdrishtva when you have the transcendental experience raso api nivartante even the desire even the sense of enjoyment goes away so it is not that he is only abstaining strictly on the basis of certain principles that no I must not one he has one who has developed paramdrishtva rasopyasya paramdrishtva nivartante rasavarjam rasopyasya paramdrishtva nivartante.

### seeing the Lord, devotional service, maturity
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/4ooHAtaPjas?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "For ordinary persons the Lord is not visible, however when one can understand the significance of his holy name and one engages himself in the devotional service of the Lord, beginning with the tongue, by chanting and tasting Prasad, then gradually the Lord reveals himself."
**Summary:** This segment introduces the verse and explains how the Lord, initially unseen by ordinary eyes, becomes visible to pure devotees through devotional service and maturity in their love for God.

In this verse we find the word Achakshat Akshavishayam. The Supreme Lord cannot be seen by ordinary eyes, but he now became visible to the eyesight of the Kumaras. Another significant word is Samadhi Bhagyam. Meditators who are very fortunate can see the Vishnu form of the Lord within their hearts by following the yogic process, but to see him face to face is a different matter. This is only possible for pure devotees. The Kumaras therefore upon seeing the Lord coming forward with his associates, who were holding an umbrella and a chamara fan, were struck with wonder and they were seeing the Lord face to face. It is said in the Brahma Samhita that devotees being elevated in love of God always see Shama Sundara, the Supreme Personality of Godhead within their hearts, but when they are mature, the same God is visible before them face to face. For ordinary persons the Lord is not visible, however when one can understand the significance of his holy name and one engages himself in the devotional service of the Lord, beginning with the tongue, by chanting and tasting Prasad, then gradually the Lord reveals himself. Thus the devotee constantly sees the Lord within his heart, and in a more mature stage, one can see the same Lord directly as we can see everything else. Thus ends the Bhaktivedanta Parbat.

---

### inaccessibility, mundane senses, analogy
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/4ooHAtaPjas?t=1086
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers, General public
**Key Quote:** "Krishna's reality, the reality of Krishna or Vishnu, is inaccessible to our mundane senses."
**Summary:** This segment uses the analogy of a mobile phone unable to make international calls to illustrate that our mundane senses have limitations and cannot access the higher reality of Krishna or Vishnu.

This understanding is presented throughout in the Vedic literatures. And Srila Prabhupada also says the same thing. He is, Krishna's reality, the reality of Krishna or Vishnu, is inaccessible to our mundane senses. Our mundane senses can only access a certain amount of reality. Not even all of the material reality, right? Our senses cannot understand. Our eyes cannot see the mind and intelligence. But we know people have mind intelligence, and they are working, and it is working. We can see the effects of the mind and intelligence, although we cannot see the mind and intelligence. So our senses have limitation. Even our mind and intelligence has limitation. What they can access in this reality as material reality. So there is a certain reality beyond what is accessible to the mind, senses and intelligence. And Krishna or Vishnu belongs to that higher reality. So our senses don't have the powers to access that realm of reality. That is the important point. Just like suppose you have a mobile phone. And your mobile phone, you don't have international, you only have facility to make local calls, India calls. You can't make any call outside of India. And somebody comes and tells you, I have a friend in America, and this is the number of my friend. And you use your phone and try to call that number. It's an American number. Call will not go through. You try many times, it will not go through. Now somebody may say, no, no, you charge properly, then it may go through. You can have charge many times, still it will not go through. Somebody may say, no, no, you change your phone version, get a upgrade, a better phone. You can get a better phone, still you try, it will not go through. Go to a place where there is very good signal, and try. You can do anything you want, anything you want, you will not get the call. Then can you say, see, I have tried so much. I don't think you have a friend in America. Or even better, I don't think there is something called America. Because if there is, I must be able to make a phone call and talk. No, it is not so. Just because our phone, our instruments cannot reach out, we cannot say such a reality does not exist.

Although the senses cannot perceive, atha shri krishna naam aadhi na bhaved grahyam indriyaihi sevon mukho hi jihvadau svayam eva sphurathi adaha. ### purification, intelligence, truth
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/4ooHAtaPjas?t=1377
**Verse References:** SB 3.9.11
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "When one's intelligence is purified, then one can perceive the transcendental reality."
**Summary:** This segment references a verse spoken by Shukadeva Goswami, explaining that by meditating on the lotus feet of the Lord and purifying one's intelligence, one can perceive the transcendental reality, a process most people don't undertake.

There are many verses in the Bhagavatam, one of them is the verse spoken by Shukadeva Goswami in his prayers, which we used to chant, or we chant sometimes. yadangri abhidhyana samadhi dhautaya dhiyanupasyanti hi tatvam atmanah samadhi dhautaya anupasyanti dhiyanupasyanti. In the Vedic literatures, like in this verse in the Bhagavatam, it is describing how anupasyanti, pasyanti means to see. The Vedic literatures talks about tatva darshi vihi, those who have seen the truth. They are seeing the truth. So there is a way to see that truth. How to see the truth? yadangri abhidhyana samadhi dhautaya dhiyanupasyanti hi tatvam atmanah atmanah tatvam. Atma here refers to Paramatma. Vishnu. Vishnu Tatva. So tatvam atmanah tatvam anupasyanti. How one can see that? yadangri abhidhyana samadhi dhautaya Angri means the lotus feet of the Lord. Angri. yadangri abhidhyana. When one does abhidhyana of Angri, the lotus feet of the Lord, and becomes mature, samadhi, reaches samadhi, fully absorbed in the lotus meditation of the lotus feet of the Lord, and by such meditation, dhauti, yadangri abhidhyana samadhi dhautaya dhautaya, dhauti means to become purified. And when one's intelligence is purified, samadhi dhautaya dhia dhautaya dhia. When one's intelligence is purified, then anupasyanti hi tatvam atmanah. This is the way one can perceive the transcendental reality. And then, in this verse, Shukadeva Goswami says, vadanti chaita kavayaya tharucham. And most people don't have this, come to this realization. Most people don't take the trouble of actually following the process, purifying the senses, purifying their consciousness by intense meditation, absorption on the lotus feet of the Lord. And hence they don't have a perception of the truth. But they still talk about the truth, and they talk in their own way, without proper understanding. That is why innumerable ideas and opinions have come about in this world about God. Those who have seen God, truly experienced God, they have one understanding, all the bona fide acharyas.

But still, his prayers are considered very special, and it has become part of the Bhagavatam, because Bhagavatam explains that he did not compose those prayers himself. Already those prayers were there in the Vedic literatures since time immemorial. And so those prayers, which were already present in the Vedic literatures, which he was trained in, so he offered those prayers, and hence hamsa guhyas prayers have a transcendental significance, and it is part of the Srimad Bhagavatam.

Hamsa, generally, hamsa in Sanskrit means pure. It also refers to the swan, which is very pure, white, pure. And that's how very exalted persons are called paramahamsas, because they are very very pure. hamsaya tasmai shucisadmane namah. shucisadma, shuchi means pure again, sadma means an abode of purity. So, this is the position that the Vedic literatures have consistently presented. In one place in the Bhagavad Gita, when Prabhupada is quoting this verse, Prabhupada translates the words, the words, sevonmukaha, as when one is spiritually saturated with transcendental service. When our consciousness is spiritually saturated, saturated, we understand that when it is completely absorbed, and nothing else is there, remember in chemistry we used to study, concentrated, saturated solution, means it won't, it is fully saturated, nothing else, you can't add any more salt and it won't dissolve anymore, because the solvent is now saturated. In the same way, when our consciousness is saturated, no material conception, no material desires, no material contaminants, no contamination, no anartha, when it is saturated, spiritually saturated, in that state, one can perceive. This is the message in the Vedic literatures consistently.

It is not for some kind of an honor and distinction and adoration and good words from other people, that's not the purpose we are here. So we should remember that it is for that transcendental spiritual experience of the Lord, which the Vedic literatures are promising, the great Acharyas are offering. It is for that. And for that, it requires a certain amount of intensity, dedication. And when we remember that, and all of these material difficulties will become very simple and trivial. ### yoga, mind control, Krishna consciousness
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/Ho8Mz4YmEyw?t=30
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Krishna consciousness is the topmost yoga system."
**Summary:** This segment explains the general yoga process, emphasizing the importance of concentrating the mind on the Supreme Personality of Godhead and highlighting Krishna consciousness as the topmost yoga system, contrasting it with voidism and impersonalism.

The general yoga process entails observing the rules and regulations, practicing the different sitting postures, concentrating the mind on the vital circulation of the air, and then thinking of the Supreme Personality of Godhead in His Vaikuntha pastimes. This is the general process of yoga. This same concentration can be achieved by other recommended processes, and therefore, Anyais Cha, other methods also can be applied. The essential point is that the mind, which is contaminated by material attractions, has to be bridled and concentrated on the Supreme Personality of Godhead. It cannot be fixed on something void or impersonal. For this reason, so-called yoga practices of voidism and impersonalism are not recommended in any standard yoga shastra. The real yogi is the devotee because his mind is always concentrated on the pastimes of Lord Krishna. Therefore, Krishna consciousness is the topmost yoga system.

---

### attraction, consciousness, sense gratification
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/Ho8Mz4YmEyw?t=882
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Attraction itself is not a wrong thing. Being attracted to Indriya Vishaya is a wrong thing."
**Summary:** This segment delves into the nature of attraction as a fundamental feature of consciousness, distinguishing between attraction to sense gratification (Indriya Vishaya) and attraction itself, and contrasting Vaishnava and Mayavadi philosophies on the role of attraction in spiritual life.

Now, this attraction. Attraction means our consciousness, something it grabs our attention, something it holds our attention, something that evokes our interest, our liking. And that's why we get attracted to something. Just like all of us have this experience. We go out in the auto or we go out in the car. When you're driving, you're looking at things outside. Immediately there are many, many, many things which attract our attention, right? Those are the objects of senses, Indriya Vishaya. It attracts us. It attracts our attention, and this attention is a feature of consciousness. This table has no attention. It has no consciousness. So moment we say there is a soul, and the soul has consciousness, and the soul has the ability to be attracted to different thing. The table is not attracted to anything. If there is an ant crawling on the floor, the ant is attracted to something and hence it is walking and crawling and heading somewhere because it is attracted. So this principle of being attracted itself is a feature of our consciousness. Now the mayavadi's approach is, this attraction is a wrong thing. The Vaishnava's philosophy is, no, no, no. Attraction itself is not a wrong thing. Being attracted to Indriya Vishaya is a wrong thing. The feature of being attracted is not a wrong thing. In fact, it is the feature of being attracted. We like it. We are drawn to it. We are charmed by it, and that's what gives us pleasure. So the feature of being attracted is not wrong. That's a feature of the consciousness. Table has no attraction. Every living entity will always have attraction.

### spiritual life, attraction, Vaishnava philosophy

**Verse References:** —

**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers

This is the kind of an understanding that the Mayavadis have. And the Vaishnavas say no, no, no. That's not the truth. Spiritual life also full of attraction, and attractive features are there in the spiritual world. And that attractive feature is between the Lord, the living entity and the Lord in the spiritual world. There are wonderful pastimes. There are wonderful situations created by Yogamaya in the spiritual world, and the living entity is a participant in all of those activities which are extremely attractive. That is the view of spiritual world and spiritual consciousness presented in the Vedic literature. A very nice verse which tells us about this is Kunti's prayers. We have all chanted this verse. You are all familiar with this verse. Kunti Devi is saying Matir Madhupate Sakrit. May Matihi, my consciousness, my mind, may it be always be drawn to Madhupate, Madhupati who is Krishna. Ananya Vishaya and no other thought, no other subject but only Krishna. And how should it be? Rati Mudvahata Daddha. Rati means attraction. So I should be drawn. I should be attracted to Krishna. How I should be attracted to Krishna? With the force, like Ganga is flowing towards the ocean. If you go to Haridwar, any of you must have seen, and when you see the Ganga flowing there, one thing you can notice is the force with which Ganga is flowing. There is some kind of a force. There is some kind of a something drawing Ganga to run, rushing towards the ocean. Kunti is praying, may my consciousness also rush towards Krishna. You see that element of attraction. When you are attracted to something, it is irresistible. You are drawn to it.

### raga-anuga bhakti, attraction, spiritual life
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/Ho8Mz4YmEyw?t=1480

**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers

We have opened a new house. Somehow finish it off, finish quickly, because they have no attraction. For them, it is some kind of a vidhi. We have to do what to do. My wife is pushing me to do. ### raga-anuga bhakti, attraction to Krishna, purification
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/Ho8Mz4YmEyw?t=1803

**Content Type:** philosophy

Actually, the word raga-anuga, anuga, ga means gamishyati, to go. Anuga means to follow. And follow what? Raga-anuga. Raga means attraction. So you will come to a stage where you will be drawn to Krishna and you will be going in that direction. That stage is called raga-anuga bhakti. Rati muddhva hata adha-gange vaugam udhanvati. It is not that Ganga is flowing down the river like that with great ferocity like that because they have put one big pump and the pump is pushing the water. No, no, no, no. No pump is required in Ganga when Ganga is flowing. Ganga is flowing spontaneously with such velocity. In the same way, we can come to a stage where our consciousness will be drawn to Krishna like that and not attracted to anything else. Another example that Chaitanya Mahaprabhupada gives is yadavadimamachetakrishna-padaravinde nava-nava-rasa-dhamya-udhyatam rantum asit tadavadibhatanarisangamesmaryamane bhavati mukhavikaraha sustu nishtivanam ca.

And when they do their duties in a detached manner, and gradually enjoy the senses, dharma, artha, kama, all of that, then gradually, when they do that, there is a certain amount of detachment that they have to practice, and that will bring about a certain enlightenment in them. It helps them to understand an all-pervading, eternal, formless absolute truth, which is called Brahman. And.

All of them so there was the karma there was the gana all of that was there but here and there there was also exalted devotee exalted personalities who knew about the direct process and the direct process is called the bhagavatam process. Bhagavatam means in connection with Bhagavan directly in connection with the Bhagavan this process was known so Vyasa Deva when he was instructed by Narada now you compile a Vedic literature now he recalled that I have myself spoken this direct process to my son Shukadeva Vyasa Deva knew that and he had spoken that to his son nam so that my son I had spoken because I saw my son he was refusing to be born come out of the mother's womb for several years and finally he came out and then after he came out he walked away I was calling out my dear son no no you're my son I have to do the regular purificatory processes but he just walked away and I was feeling great separation and I was calling putra iti I was calling out my dear son my dear son all the tree all the trees that were there all reflected my words and they also called out putra putra iti in other words the trees were echoing and the son walked away so then I realized my son is a very exalted person and so I have to teach him the very exalted message the highest direct process and I taught him the bhagavatam and he learned it.
