There was another occasion Pariksit he was cursed to die in seven days and when he renounced the kingdom and he was preparing to die many sages came and Pariksit asked him what is the process what is the duty of a man about to die and they all were coming up with different ideas there was a lot of confusion some were saying Dhyana some were saying you should do Arunashrama some were saying no no you should not do that some were saying no no you should not do that some were saying no no you should not do that some were saying no no you should not do that you should do something else and there was confused at that time Shukadeva came and Shukadeva knew the bhagavatam and he spoke and everyone's became silent and said yes what he is saying that's the ultimate thing suitable for a great person like Pariksit and there that conversation happened so like this there were many many occasions where Yama Raj spoke to Yama Dootas when the Yama Raj Yamadūtas tried to conquer Ajāmila and they could not. Some other strange personalities came and stopped them and they went back to Yamarāja and asked, what is this happening? And then Yamarāja told them, the bhāgavata knowledge. So like this, Vyāsadeva compiles all those instances where the bhāgavata knowledge, the direct process was explained by great personalities and all of those he compiled together and formed the bhāgavatam. ### direct process, pure devotee, chanting
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/wXJ0bnY4EUg?t=1904

**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers

Now for the direct process to work, one or two important features are required. If you take all of these examples, when Śukadeva was instructed by Vedavyasa, Parīkṣit was instructed by Śukadeva, the sages of Naimishāraṇyā were instructed by Suta Gosvāmī or Yamadūtas were instructed by Yamarāja. And so many, Dhruva was instructed by Nārada. Like that, many, many examples if you take. In all of these, for the bhāgavata process, the direct quick process to work, one important feature is, you must come in touch with a pure devotee who knows Kṛṣṇa, who has that intimate understanding of Kṛṣṇa. That is the trigger for the direct process. And not always easy. And so bhāgavatam process for it to work, we have to come in touch with a pure devotee and serve a pure devotee. And another important feature for the bhāgavata process to work, which is an accelerated process, direct process, and that requirement is to chant the holy name of the Lord, to come in touch with the Lord directly. And for Kali Yuga, the Lord has appeared in the form of holy name and to chant the holy name.

### devotional service, knowledge, surrender
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/wXJ0bnY4EUg?t=2002
**Verse References:** BG 9.2
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Devotional service in Kṛṣṇa consciousness is the direct method."
**Summary:** This segment summarizes a purport explaining the two kinds of devotional service: regulated principles and full attachment, and emphasizes that Kṛṣṇa consciousness is the direct method, while the indirect method involves renunciation, knowledge, and meditation.

This whole thing is described in a very succinct manner. In this purport, I will read this one. As mentioned in the previous verses, there are two kinds of devotional service. The way of regulated principles and the way of full attachment in love to the Supreme Personality of Godhead. This is referring to the ultimate process. There are two kinds of devotional service: the way of regulated principles and the way of full attachment. The full attachment is having full bhakti, highest level of prema bhakti. If you cannot do that, to achieve that, you have to do regulated bhakti. For those who are actually not able to follow the principles of Kṛṣṇa consciousness, it is better to cultivate knowledge, because by knowledge, one can be able to understand his real position. Gradually, knowledge will develop to the point of meditation. Jnana to meditation. By meditation, one can be able to understand the Supreme Personality of Godhead by a gradual process. There are processes which make one understand that one himself is the Supreme, and that sort of meditation is preferred. One is unable to engage in devotional service. If one is not able to meditate in such a way, then there are prescribed duties as enjoined in the Vedic literature, for the brāhmaṇas, vaiśyas, śūdras, which we shall find later in the chapter of Bhagavad-gītā. Now coming back to the karma-pala-tyāga. One should give up the results of chapter of Bhagavad-gītā. But in all cases, one should give up the result or fruits of labor. This means to employ the result of karma for some good cause, like hospitals and such charities. In summary, to reach the Supreme Personality of Godhead, the highest goal, there are two processes. One process is by gradual development, and the other process is direct. Devotional service in Kṛṣṇa consciousness is the direct method. And the other method involves renouncing the fruits of one's activities. Then one can come to the stage of knowledge, then to the stage of meditation, then to the stage of understanding the Supersoul, and then to the stage of the Supreme Personality of Godhead. One may either take the step-by-step process or the indirect path. The direct process is not possible for everyone. Therefore, the indirect process is also good. It is, however, to be understood that the indirect process is not recommended for Arjuna, because he is already a saint. He is already at the stage of loving devotional service to the Supreme Lord. It is for others who are not at this stage. For them, the gradual process of renunciation, knowledge, meditation, and realization of the Supersoul and Brahman should be followed. But as far as Bhagavad-gītā is concerned, it is the direct method that is stressed. Everyone is advised to take to the direct method and surrender unto the Supreme Personality of Godhead, Kṛṣṇa.

---

So, this is the process that is recommended by Caitanya Mahāprabhu. And this is the process that the entire Bhagavatam is all about. How to take the direct process? And that was further summarized by Caitanya Mahāprabhu as Sādhanabhakti. And that leads to Rāgānuga Bhakti. And as we advance in Rāgānuga Bhakti, we come to the highest stage. The highest stages of Prema Bhakti. One will have complete understanding of the Absolute Truth. So, this is the overall picture that we get. And so, in that sense, we see that Dhyāna, Dhyāna was recommended, like Kapila is mentioning, because it was more suitable for other ages. Valmiki did, Dhruva did, and all of these examples are there because it was suitable for another age. And one could make gradual progress in understanding Paramātmā and then the ability to transfer to Vaikuṇṭha Loka. And Krishna had just then appeared, 5000 years ago. And so, Vyāsadeva wanted to disclose about Krishna's activities. And among them, the Vraja activities, Krishna's activities, for those 10 years and 7 months, when He was in Vrindavan, those are considered even more exalted because there He exhibited the Madhurya Bhakti, pure Madhurya Bhakti. And so, those are also very, very confidential aspects and Vyāsadeva explains all of that. So, like this, Chaitanya Mahāprabhu helps us to get an overview of the whole Vedic process, how, what falls into, where all these things fall into place, and what is the position of Bhakti, what is the position of the Bhagavatam process. We'll stop here. Grantharāja Śrīmad Bhāgavatam ki Śrīla Prabhupāda ki.

## The Lord in the Heart as a Witness | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### Krishna consciousness, witness, surveillance
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/p8kADDM697s?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Krishna is seated in the heart and he is watching."
**Summary:** The speaker uses the analogy of CCTV surveillance to explain how Krishna is always watching us from within our hearts.

You go to a big store and there'll be CCTVs in different places. They'll put a board: "This area is under CCTV surveillance." That means they put a CCTV and they're informing you somebody could be watching or somebody is recording. And if we see such a board there, this is a CCTV surveillance zone. We are careful. We become alert. We don't do some wrong things, right? In the Bhagavatam, it is said Krishna is the witness of the innermost core of our heart. And the highest yogi is one who is devoted to Krishna in the innermost core of his heart. That is why in Bhakti, we cannot cheat at all. We may cheat externally, others, but Krishna is seated in the heart and he is watching. So we are always in the surveillance zone of Krishna. Nothing is out of his purview.

---

About two years ago, if you had asked somebody, a young person, what is the theory of everything, से सेलियों के बाद रहे हैं। उम्मीद करें कि यह आज एक भारतिल फॉलाफिकल फिल्म है स्तीफेन हार्किंग का सोचता था। और उसको आगे बाद भी बढ़कर हुआ है। इस वर्ष का साथ स्टीफेन हार्किंग आफ्ट यॉराइस्ड है। world this name theory of everything, he is not the one who coined it. The theory of everything is a is a mathematical scientific framework which scientists have been working, if I remember right, maybe last 80 years. I remember as a college student attending a lecture in Bangalore City and those days it was known as the grand unification theory. Basically it's like this: scientists have figured out that there are four fundamental forces of nature. There is the gravitational force, the electromagnetic force, and two of them called the nuclear force. One is called a strong nuclear force and other is a weak one nuclear force. Basically these four forces have come into play and led to the world as we see it today, whether it's the stars, the galaxies, and the black hole, or whether it's elements and all the things that we see in close proximity on our planet. And according to scientists, even the evolution of life has all happened because of these four forces. And now what scientists have been trying to do is, is there a way that these four distinct forces can further be united to come to one which has led to the four forces which has led to the world and the universe? This is known as the grand unification theory and scientists have been working on this all over the world. And at some point this theory, if it can explain everything, because that's one force or whatever that is which led to these four forces and these four forces has led to the entire cosmos that we see including us. And we are talking about all of these things, it is something that should be able to explain everything. And that was the grand unification theory and that became more popular by Stephen Hawking. Stephen Hawking was not only a brilliant scientist, he was also a great popularizer of science and so that's how this his biographical film came to

**Summary:** The speaker explains the meaning of 'Veda' as knowledge and how Vyasadeva compiled and structured Vedic knowledge, culminating in Vedanta as the ultimate or end of all knowledge.

and he was writing a letter to the Prime Minister of the country at that time soliciting some help from the Prime Minister and now let's go to this subject, what is the Vedanta message and you would have all come across this in Prabhupada's books the word Veda it means to know or to or knowledge it comes from the root word in Sanskrit with with actually and with means to know or and the word Veda means knowledge and so actually when Vyasadeva was compiling the Vedas he was not thinking that I am compiling a certain set of beliefs of the Hindus he was compiling the knowledge that was prevalent and was being transmitted from generation to generation in an oral tradition and that knowledge at the dawn of Kali Yuga he was compiling that into a written form and that came to be known as Veda. Now what Vyasadeva did was he was not only compiling the knowledge and he was creating a hierarchical structure for knowledge because every knowledge has basic knowledge, a more advanced knowledge, a most advanced and the most advanced knowledge, just like say for instance you take mathematics that is basic mathematics we all studied in school and then high school mathematics then we studied a little more mathematics in college and then if you do your masters and your PhD in mathematics and it will be very very advanced mathematics. So in knowledge there is a hierarchical structure as we begin to comprehend and appreciate and able to understand more and more of it you can go to higher and higher levels of learning and that's very true with the philosophy philosophical knowledge the very basic knowledge and so he created hierarchical stages of knowledge and he Vyasadeva wrote the most advanced part of the Vedic knowledge in the form of Vedanta. Anta means the end or the ultimate and so Vedanta actually means the ultimate or the end of all knowledge and that is about Vedanta and it was that knowledge of Vedanta which Srila Prabhupada found that to be very fundamental universal powerful basic and this should benefit everyone in the world and that was the driving force and that was the instruction he had received from his spiritual master and his spiritual master and so on so this is the Vedanta knowledge and which is considered even among the Vedic knowledge the ultimate or the end of all knowledge

### Vedanta, Bhagavad Gita, Vedic Wisdom
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/c6T8cIJthGg?t=1082
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Vedanta is the last word in Vedic wisdom so you can imagine that there is a certain Vedic wisdom it's put in the form of the Vedas the Puranas the Upanishads and all of that and the last word in that is the Vedanta"
**Summary:** The speaker describes Vedanta as the last word in Vedic wisdom, summarized by Krishna to Arjuna in the Bhagavad Gita.

now what is the Vedanta knowledge about? Prabhupada writes in one of the purports Vedanta is the last word in Vedic wisdom. So you can imagine that there is a certain Vedic wisdom it's put in the form of the Vedas, the Puranas, the Upanishads and all of that and the last word in that is the Vedanta very important. And in fact that Vedanta knowledge was summarized by Krishna to Arjuna in the Bhagavad Gita that's why the Bhagavad Gita becomes extremely important because in a very succinct manner the Lord himself spoke that Vedanta, the last word of Vedic wisdom in the form of the Bhagavad Gita and and later on we hear from Srila Prabhupada and from Chaitanya Mahaprabhu's explanation and the Vedanta that Vyasa Deva wrote was in the form of Sutras we will talk about that a little while later also that's how it is known as the Vedanta Sutras or also known as Brahma Sutra. So Vedanta Sutras are in the form of Sutras. Sutras are very very short statements which are not always following grammatical rules so it is agrammatical it's very concise it is full of meaning because those days there were no hard disks and search engines and all of those kind of things and so people had to memorize they could easily commit to memory these Sutras and you can walk around anywhere and then pull out a Sutra from your memory and then open it up expand on it. So all of these things were possible and that's how Sutra is another kind of a composition in Sanskrit literature you not only have prose you not only have poetry you have drama you have place there is another kind of a literary structure in Sanskrit known as the Sutras and these are very very concise and it is compressed with meaning it is meant for insiders it's not necessarily outsiders may not understand they require commentaries and explanations of that. So this is the Vedanta Sutras and Vyasadeva compiled Vedanta the last word of Vedic wisdom in the form of Sutras

### Cause and Effect, Material Cause, Multiple Causes
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/c6T8cIJthGg?t=2263
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "for any effect like an earthen pot is an effect there are multiple causes which makes it happen"
**Summary:** The speaker uses the example of an earthen pot to illustrate the concept of multiple causes, including material, instrumental, and efficient causes.

is something that's very common. Now let's take one example cause effect analysis what is the cause of an earthen pot so we are all familiar with an earthen pot what is its cause someone came up and said ah come on I know what is the cause of an earthen pot it's the earth because it's the earth that was made into a pot someone else said ah no no no it was the potter's wheel if you have earth and you don't have a potter's wheel how will you get a pot it will just remain as Earth so you need a potter's wheel and the potter's wheel is actually the cause of the pot then someone else came up and said no not the earth not the potter's wheel it was actually the potter if there was no potter if there is earth and there is a potter's wheel and if there is no potter where will you have a pot so it's actually it's the potter who is actually the cause of an Earth of an earthen pot so this kind of analysis and actually there are different kinds of causes what is known as a material cause an instrumental cause an efficient cause so the earth is the material cause potter's wheel is also a cause it's an instrumental cause and the potter himself is an efficient cause so in other words we are beginning to see that for any effect like an earthen pot is an effect there are multiple causes which makes it happen

### Cause and Effect, Chain of Causes, Vedanta
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/c6T8cIJthGg?t=3117
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "in our quest for cause of an effect we come across an absurd phenomena or an effect but that phenomena has a cause an identifiable cause but that cause itself is an effect and is caused by another identifiable cause and that's caused by another cause its cause its cause and so on"
**Summary:** The speaker introduces the principle of the chain of causes, using the example of a cool breeze to illustrate how any effect can be traced back to a series of causes, each of which is itself an effect.

that the vedanta philosophy does. Now we will do one more analysis of the cause and effect which is there in the vedic literatures in the vedanta philosophy let's take one example suppose I am feeling some cool breeze now the cool breeze is an effect now I can analyze what is the cause of the cool breeze and I will find the effect to be there is a fan and the fan is bringing this cool breeze that I am experiencing the fan itself is an effect and it is caused by electricity so if I if the cool breeze is caused by the fan and the fan is fan itself is an effect fan is caused by electricity and electricity itself is an effect and that is caused by a generator which is producing the electricity now I can say so you may say that the generator is the cause of the electricity but I will say yeah it's cause of the electricity but generator itself is an effect it is caused by something else probably waterfalls and hydroelectric plant or so on and now now we may say the waterfall is the cause of the generator I will say no the water call is cause it's waterfall itself is an effect there is a cause for that and we may say that is sorry that's the rain cloud what is the cause of the rainfall and you can say the sun and so on so in other words you can see in this world any effect so in our quest for cause of an effect we come across an absurd phenomena or an effect but that phenomena has a cause an identifiable cause but that cause itself is an effect and is caused by another identifiable cause and that's caused by another cause its cause its cause and so on so we come across another principle that's operating in this world called the principle of chain of causes

### Multiple Causes, Chain of Causes, Absolute Truth
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/c6T8cIJthGg?t=3258
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "the world or the universe we live in is a complex web of causes and effects on the time dimension so these causes are themselves effects caused by another layer of causes and that caused by another layer in other words the whole universe that we observe is a complex web of causes and effects on the time dimension"
**Summary:** The speaker combines the principles of multiple causes and the chain of causes to describe the universe as a complex web of interconnected causes and effects, setting the stage for further discussion on absolute truth.

### Cause and effect, Ultimate cause, Engine analogy
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/evLBY6yRyDA?t=550
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Trying to find the ultimate cause which is not dependent on any other cause, but can cause all other causes, this is actually the search that is going on in the Vedanta philosophy."
**Summary:** Using the analogy of a train, this segment explains the concept of cause and effect, emphasizing the search for the ultimate cause that is independent and the source of all other causes within Vedanta philosophy.

Now Srila Prabhupada gives an interesting example of this in one Conversations which is recorded in the book Life Comes from Life. Prabhupada gives this example: suppose you are sitting in a train bogie and that bogie is moving, that's the effect, a bogie is moving and your question will be why is my bogie moving? A quick answer is there is another bogie in front of your bogie and that's pulling it and hence your bogie is moving, fair enough, accurate, correct, rational, scientific answer. Now we will shift the question, why is that bogie moving? We will get an answer that bogie is moving because there is another bogie in front of it that is pulling it, fair enough. We shift our question, why is that bogie moving? You will say another bogie is moving and on and on and on and finally you will say you will come to an engine, a locomotive engine which is pulling all of these bogies. Then you will say very good, now tell me what is moving the cause of the locomotive engine that is moving all of this? Is there another bogie in front of it which is pulling the locomotive engine? Hey no no no, an engine doesn't require something else to be pulling it. An engine is such that it can pull all the bogies and also can pull itself. That's why all the bogies are in one category, engine is of another category altogether and engine doesn't require anything else, it is by itself able to move and can cause the movement of all other bogies. So this is the cause effect cause effect and trying to find the ultimate cause which is not dependent on any other cause but can cause all other causes, this is actually the search that is going on in the Vedanta philosophy.

**Content Type:** philosophy

**Key Quote:** "We find two categories of creation, two categories of truth, two categories of existence: one is the sentient existence, sentient meaning conscious, with cognitive functions like perceptions, feelings, desires, emotions, and with personal attributes; another category of existence that we see in the creation is insentient existence, which is lacking consciousness, perceptions, lacking cognitive functions, impersonal or lacking personality."
**Summary:** This segment categorizes creation into sentient (conscious) and insentient (lacking consciousness) existence, stating that both originate from the absolute truth.

we find two categories of creation, two categories of truth, two categories of existence. One is the sentient existence, sentient meaning conscious with cognitive functions like perceptions, feelings, desires, emotions, and with personal attributes like all of us are human beings. Not just human beings, even animals, they also are conscious, they are sentient. Even an ant is sentient, it is conscious, it has cognitive functions, it has feelings, emotions, desires, aspirations, goals in life, all of these things. So this is one category of sentient existence. Another category of existence that we see in the creation is insentient existence, which is lacking consciousness, perceptions, lacking cognitive functions, impersonal or lacking personality, just like the table, the building, the mountains, the river, land, and all of these things. This is also part of this creation. So broadly, this creation has two kinds of categories of creation: one is the sentient and the insentient. Now, both categories of creation have come from the absolute truth. That's the Vedanta Sutra Janma Dhyasya Yatha, that truth from which all of this creation has come, meaning both categories of creation have come from that absolute truth. Now it's a simple logic, the cause should be more than the effect. Like, say for example, we look at the sun and we see the sun is so bright, so much heat, and the sunshine is coming from the sun and we see the sunshine is so bright and so hot, so it has got heat and light. Now what can we say about the source of the sunlight, the sun?

### Krishna, Source of everything, Superior energy
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/evLBY6yRyDA?t=3046
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Inferior energy has no power unless superior energy is involved."
**Summary:** This segment quotes Srila Prabhupada, stating that Krishna is the source of everything and that inferior energy is dependent on superior energy, using the analogy of an engineer controlling a train to illustrate Krishna's role in the cosmic manifestation.

And Srila Prabhupada points out, "Lord Krishna is the source of everything, *aham sarvasya prabhavaha*." And thus, the end of all knowledge, Vedanta. In this world, there may be knowledge, and the end of all knowledge is to know the Lord, to know our relationship with Him, and to act according to that relationship only, because we have no other work, we have no other business in this world. We only, the truth is that Krishna is there, and we are caused by Him, from Him we have come, and we have a relationship, and we must act in that relationship. So we are offered from various sources, as I mentioned earlier, in the book *Life Comes From Life* by Srila Prabhupada, Prabhupada mentions this. Srila Prabhupada, inferior energy has no power unless superior energy is involved. This sea, indicating the Pacific, Prabhupada was taking a walk in the morning in Los Angeles, and he is pointing out, indicating the Pacific Ocean is calm and quiet, but when the superior force, air, pushes it, it manifests high waves. The ocean has no power to move without the superior force of air. Similarly, there is another force superior to the air, and another, and another, and ultimately we arrive at Krishna. This is real research. Krishna controls nature just as an engineer controls a train. The engineer controls a locomotive which pulls one car, and that car in turn pulls another, which pulls another, and so the whole train is moving. Similarly with the creation, Krishna gives the first push, and then by means of successive pushes, the entire cosmic manifestation comes into being and is maintained.

### Material nature, Seed-giving father, Krishna
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/evLBY6yRyDA?t=3172
**Verse References:** BG 9.10, BG 14.4
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "This material nature is working under my direction and is producing all moving and non-moving beings."
**Summary:** This segment quotes Krishna from the Bhagavad Gita, explaining that material nature works under His direction and that He is the seed-giving father, the primary cause of everything, while scientists only observe intermediate causes.

This is explained in the Bhagavad Gita, "This material nature is working under my direction and is producing all moving and non-moving beings." And in the fourteenth chapter Krishna says, *sarvayon nishukam teya murtaya sambhavantiya tasam brahma mahad yonir aham bija pradham pitah*, "All species of life are made possible even by birth in this material nature, O son of Kunti, and I am the seed giving father." For example, if we sow a banyan seed, a huge tree eventually comes up, and along with it millions of new seeds. Each of these seeds can in turn produce another tree with millions of new seeds, and so on. This is how Krishna, the original seed giving father, is the primary cause of everything we see. Unfortunately, the scientists observe only the intermediate cause. They cannot perceive the remote cause. Krishna is described in the Vedas as *sarvakarana karanam*, the cause of all causes. If one understands the cause of all causes, then he understands everything, *yasmin vignate sarvam evam vignatam bhavati* Upanishad. If one knows the original cause, the subordinate causes are automatically known. Although the scientists are searching after the original cause, when the Vedas, perfect knowledge, declare the original cause to be the supreme personality of Godhead, the scientists won't accept it. They keep to their partial imperfect knowledge. This is their disease. All this Prabhupada is telling in that morning walk conversation.

---
### Prasthana Traya, Absolute truth, Krishna

**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "The demigods give information that the absolute supreme absolute truth is Krishna."

There is another reference from Chaitanya Charita Amruta. According to learned scholars, there are three different sources of knowledge which are called Prasthana Traya. According to these scholars, Vedanta is one such source for its presence, Vedic knowledge on the basis of logic and sound arguments. In the Bhagavad Gita, the Lord says, *Brahma Sutra Pada is Chai Vahet Umad Pir Vini Shchitai Vini Shchitai Hi*, understanding of the ultimate goal of life is ascertained in the Brahma Sutra by legitimate logic and argument concerning cause and effect. That's what we have been discussing yesterday and today, causes and effects and all of these things. There is another reference, this is too fine, and I think I'll read this slowly. Then the demigods address the Lord as *Satyam Param*, or the supreme absolute truth. Everyone is searching after the truth, that is a philosophical way of life. The demigods give information that the absolute supreme absolute truth is Krishna. One who becomes fully Krishna conscious can attain the absolute truth. Krishna is the absolute truth because unlike relative truth, he is the truth in all three phases of eternal time. Time is divided into past, present, and future. Krishna is truth always, past, present, and future, being controlled by supreme time in the course of past, present, and future. But before the creation, Krishna was existing, and when there is creation, everything is resting in Krishna, and when this creation is finished, Krishna will remain. Therefore, he is the absolute truth in all circumstances. If there is any truth within this material world, it emanates from that supreme truth, Krishna. If there is any opulence within this material world, the cause of the opulence is Krishna. If there is any reputation within this material world, the cause of the reputation is Krishna. If there is any strength within this material world, the cause of such strength is Krishna. If there is any wisdom and education within this material world, the cause of such wisdom and education is Krishna. Therefore, Krishna is the source of all relative truth, so...

Krishna is the absolute truth because unlike relative truth, he is the truth in all three phases of eternal time. Time is divided into past, present, and future. Krishna is truth always, past, present, and future. In the material world, everything is being controlled by supreme time in the course of past, present, and future, but before the creation Krishna was existing and when there is creation everything is resting in Krishna and when this creation is finished Krishna will remain therefore he is the absolute truth in all circumstances. If there is any truth within this material world it emanates from that supreme truth Krishna. If there is any opulence within this material world the cause of the opulence is Krishna. If there is any reputation within this material world the cause of the reputation is Krishna. If there is any strength within this material world the cause of such strength is Krishna. If there is any wisdom and education within this material world the cause of such wisdom and education is Krishna. Therefore Krishna is the source of all relative truth. So with this we come to the end of the presentation and I think yesterday and today some devotees have raised some questions and yesterday also I went through there were a few questions and if you have more questions you can send those questions in our next session we will have a Q and A on the theory of everything the Vedanta perspective the absolute truth relative truth we will have a complete session on question and answer on this particular topic with this we will come to the end of this session thank you very much nice being with all of you I hope you all like the understanding of the absolute truth Krishna, the hermeneutics of the Bhagavatam as given by Chaitanya Mahaprabhu and Srila Prabhupada Hare Krishna Krishna, the hermeneutics of the Bhagavatam as given by Chaitanya Mahaprabhu and Srila Prabhupada

## Three Dangerous Diversions from Bhakti-yoga | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### bhakti-yoga, diversions, karma, mukti, yogasiddhi
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/j8IUXnNznv8?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "If you are able to somehow resist the temptation of these three exits, then you can head towards the supreme personality of Godhead."
**Summary:** The speaker uses the analogy of driving on an expressway to illustrate how karma, mukti, and yogasiddhi can be diversions from the path of bhakti-yoga.

You're driving on the expressway, you're heading very quickly, but then you see exit, food court, and so you exit, and then you'll see so many different kinds of food all displayed there, and then you get absorbed and lost there, and then you missed the purpose that you were heading in the expressway. So, the shastras point out, when you are trying to advance in the mission of human life, you will encounter three exits. The first exit is called karma. The second exit is called mukti, and the third exit is called yogasiddhi. If you are not careful, you can take that exit, and you can be lost there completely, and forget coming back to the exit. So, you're driving on the expressway, and heading towards the goal that you set out. If you are able to somehow resist the temptation of these three exits, then you can head towards the supreme personality of Godhead. Because, if you want to associate with Krishna, you should be free from the temptations of karma, jnana, and yogasiddhi. That is a pure devotee, who only wants to serve Krishna. He is Krishna.

Next thing the Vedic literatures are pointing out. Now this Ahankara can come under three kinds of influence: Sattva, Rajas and Tamas. And this verse is discussing about this Ahankara under the influence of Rajas. Rajoguna. The most important thing that Rajoguna does is, it puts us in a framework as I am an enjoyer. So, I am an enjoyer. I must enjoy. Now I have a body. I must enjoy with this body. Sattva Guna creates a certain kind of an understanding. It enlightens. But usually in the material world, Sattva Guna is never alone. It gets mixed with Rajoguna. So, with a certain kind of an enlightened outlook, we try to become enjoyer. And it is not just that, Sattva Guna and Rajoguna mix. There is also always an element of Tamoguna. And Tamoguna's influence is to create ignorance. So, a sense of enlightenment and knowledge and understanding with the fundamental desire to enjoy, but not covered with a certain amount of ignorance.

You see? That's why Prabhupada says in the purport here, the living condition in material existence depends more or less on one's intelligence and powerful living energy. Intelligence to counteract the hard struggle for existence is assisted by the senses for acquiring knowledge. And the living energy maintains himself by manipulating the active organs, like the hands and legs. But on the whole, the struggle for existence is an exertion of the mode of passion. We are not these human bodies. We have got a human body. We see around us, there are so many other non-human bodies also. And there are living entities there also. So, this passion, knowledge, and ignorance, combine together, in different ways, and create the material world, of which we are also part.

Vedas describe in a very poetic way that how you can enjoy now and in future in swargaloka. These are called poetic descriptions in the Vedic literature. Flowery, pushpitam vajam, Krishna says in the Gita, flowery words. This is the kavita refers to fruity activities described in the Vedic literatures. ### Bhakti, Krishna's Pleasure, Constitutional Position
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/bpXAJdRP-d4?t=1488
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Our focus is not our enjoyment, our focus is Krishna's enjoyment."
**Summary:** This segment clarifies that pure bhakti focuses on Krishna's pleasure, not personal enjoyment, and emphasizes that serving Krishna is the natural, constitutional activity of the soul.

So, in pure, so somebody may say, oh with pure bhakti, you will get bhakti, ananda of bhakti, no? That is the natural ananda, in that, the specific thing about bhakti is, our focus is not our enjoyment, our focus is Krishna's enjoyment. And as a result of serving Krishna, giving pleasure to Krishna, I may get happiness, I may not get happiness, it doesn't matter. Whether I am in heaven or hell, I simply want an opportunity to please Krishna. This is a new mode. But of course, we are constituted in such a way that when we serve Krishna, we get happiness naturally. The other methods were not natural to our constitution. Just like, if the hand puts food into the stomach, the hand gets nourished. Natural. But the hand putting the food in the stomach is a natural constitutional activity. But if the hand says, no, I won't put food in the stomach, I'll only be touching the food. I'll only be mixing rice, chapati, dal, and just, I won't, why should I feed the stomach? Stomach should enjoy, is it? No, I won't allow. Only I'll be touching. Or I'll be only seeing food. We know that won't nourish us. You see, in the same way, all attempts of karma, all attempts of jnana, are attempts for happiness in an unconstitutional manner. Constitutional meaning, Swaroopa, our makeup, how we are made, how we are constituted. This is the most important thing that we learn in Krishna consciousness. That we are not the enjoyers.

### Krishna as Enjoyer, Service, Disease
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/bpXAJdRP-d4?t=1628
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** analogy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers
**Key Quote:** "Krishna alone is the enjoyer."
**Summary:** Using the analogy of the body and its parts, this segment explains that Krishna is the ultimate enjoyer, and our role is to serve Him, just as the hands and legs serve the body. A diseased condition arises when we become uncooperative and unwilling to serve Krishna's pleasure.

Krishna is the enjoyer. Krishna alone is the enjoyer. We have only business is to make him happy. Just like the hands, only business is to keep the body in a comfortable situation. We want to have bath, the hands and the legs will work to give bath. We want to dress up, we want to put tilak, hands and legs assist me to put the tilak. We want to eat, hands and legs help. See how hands and legs are parts of the body, they are constantly working for the upkeep and well-being of the whole body. If hands and legs don't cooperate, it is called a diseased condition. We have to go to a doctor, we have to take some treatment, we have to take some treatment. Hand is not working, I am not able to lift my hand, I can't bend, fold my hand. Oh, you have to go to your doctor, you should examine. See hand is not able to work for the whole. Today our material situation is, we are also components, parts of Krishna, but we are the diseased, uncooperative, unwilling to serve the pleasure, for the pleasure of Krishna. This is our situation. We are that ailing arm. We are the diseased part of the body. This is what we have become today. This is our position. And this is coming because of our spirit of enjoyment. And that spirit of enjoyment is not natural to us. It is infused through the Rajoguna.

### Pleasure to Krishna, Remembrance, Self-Purification

And otherwise, our intent is to only give pleasure to Krishna. So, this enjoying tendency created by passion, how this is all brought about, is what this verse is describing. So, and by discussing among ourselves, and by telling others, because when we are telling others, first person who is hearing is ourself. I am giving class, but the first hearer is, some of you may slightly doze off a little, you won't, something you may miss. But one person who is not missing anything, very attentively hearing the class, is myself. So it is for my own purification. So, we speak in different kinds of forum, one on one, one to many, or different ways, mean our purification, self-purification, self-purification. This is the most important thing that we should try for. Let's stop here.

**Summary:** This segment addresses a question about the location of lust, explaining that while senses may seem dead, they are energized by Prana Shakti, which originates from the contaminated consciousness of the soul. Lust ultimately resides in the consciousness but manifests through mind, intelligence, and senses.

## Who Truly Owns Everything? | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa @ChanchalapathiDas
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### ownership, detachment, surrender
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/gjUWKTLaLSU?t=0
**Verse References:** BG 9.4, Isha Upanishad 1
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "We must use all of this to serve Rama."
**Summary:** This segment establishes the central idea that everything, including our bodies and senses, belongs to Sri Rama, and we should use them in His service.

I have come into this world, I have this Panchabhuta Sharira, Antribhuta Sharira, Sukshma Sharira. To whom all this belongs? Am I the owner of all this? Am I the owner of this body and the owner of the senses? Am I the owner of myself? To whom do I belong? Oh, we have this body, whatever strength we have, may not be much, but all of this belongs to Sri Rama, and we all belong to Sri Rama. We must use all of this to serve Rama. This is the thinking of a Bhatta. This world belongs to the Lord. Isha Vasya Midam Sarvam. Everything that is there, everything, the Lord is the owner. The Lord is the owner. The Lord is the owner.

---

## Who is a Paramahamsa? | Sri Chanchalapathi Dasa  @ChanchalapathiDas
**Speaker:** HG Chanchalapathi Dasa

### Paramahamsa, detachment, Krishna Bhakti
**Timestamp:** https://youtu.be/MVHjpcwTGxY?t=0
**Verse References:** —
**Content Type:** philosophy
**Audience:** Full-time devotees, Congregation / volunteers, Newcomers
**Key Quote:** "Unless one comes to the stage of Paramahamsa, one cannot experience Krishna Bhakti in its full form."
**Summary:** The speaker defines Paramahamsa as a stage of detachment from the material world, necessary for experiencing Krishna Bhakti, and applicable to all individuals regardless of their social role.

Rishabhadeva, Paramahamsa in Avadhoota Vesha, he appeared. Unless one comes to the stage of Paramahamsa, one cannot experience Krishna Bhakti in its full form. Paramahamsa stage, where you are uncaring for the material world. You don't care for honour, dishonour, pleasure. You are no more searching for pleasure in this material world. Bhagavatam describes Parikshit Maharaj, who was an emperor, was a Paramahamsa. He was in kingly robes. Prabhupada writes, Paramahamsa is required in every field of human activity. Because Paramahamsa always thinks, how I can do good for others. But this Paramahamsa Dharma can be practiced in other ways. In Avadhoota Vesha also, somebody who is a ruler, he should be a Paramahamsa. Somebody who is a businessman, he should be a Paramahamsa. Somebody who is a housewife, she should be a Paramahamsa. Somebody who is a child, child can also be a Paramahamsa, like Prahalad Dhruvavahar. That should be the goal of human life, to come to the Paramahamsa stage. Because in that Paramahamsa stage, one can actually experience that attraction to Krishna.

---
